  Done with indoor complaints, libraries, querulous criticisms,<br />
  Strong and content I travel the open road.

  The earth, that is sufficient,<br />
  I do not want the constellations any nearer,<br />
  I know they are very well where they are,<br />
  I know they suffice for those who belong to them.

  (Still here I carry my old delicious burdens,<br />
  I carry them, men and women, I carry them with me wherever I go,<br />
  I swear it is impossible for me to get rid of them,<br />
  I am fill'd with them, and I will fill them in return.)

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  You road I enter upon and look around, I believe you are not all<br />
<span class='indent' />that is here,<br />
  I believe that much unseen is also here.

  Here the profound lesson of reception, nor preference nor denial,<br />
  The black with his woolly head, the felon, the diseas'd, the<br />
<span class='indent' />illiterate person, are not denied;<br />
  The birth, the hasting after the physician, the beggar's tramp, the<br />
<span class='indent' />drunkard's stagger, the laughing party of mechanics,<br />
  The escaped youth, the rich person's carriage, the fop, the eloping couple,<br />
  The early market-man, the hearse, the moving of furniture into the<br />
<span class='indent' />town, the return back from the town,<br />
  They pass, I also pass, any thing passes, none can be interdicted,<br />
  None but are accepted, none but shall be dear to me.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  You air that serves me with breath to speak!<br />
  You objects that call from diffusion my meanings and give them shape!<br />
  You light that wraps me and all things in delicate equable showers!<br />
  You paths worn in the irregular hollows by the roadsides!<br />
  I believe you are latent with unseen existences, you are so dear to me.

  You flagg'd walks of the cities! you strong curbs at the edges!<br />
  You ferries! you planks and posts of wharves! you timber-lined<br />
<span class='indent' />side! you distant ships!<br />
  You rows of houses! you window-pierc'd facades! you roofs!<br />
  You porches and entrances! you copings and iron guards!<br />
  You windows whose transparent shells might expose so much!<br />
  You doors and ascending steps! you arches!<br />
  You gray stones of interminable pavements! you trodden crossings!<br />
  From all that has touch'd you I believe you have imparted to<br />
<span class='indent' />yourselves, and now would impart the same secretly to me,<br />
  From the living and the dead you have peopled your impassive surfaces,<br />
<span class='indent' />and the spirits thereof would be evident and amicable with me.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  The earth expanding right hand and left hand,<br />
  The picture alive, every part in its best light,<br />
  The music falling in where it is wanted, and stopping where it is<br />
<span class='indent' />not wanted,<br />
  The cheerful voice of the public road, the gay fresh sentiment of the road.

  O highway I travel, do you say to me Do not leave me?<br />
  Do you say Venture not if you leave me you are lost?<br />
  Do you say I am already prepared, I am well-beaten and undenied,<br />
<span class='indent' />adhere to me?

  O public road, I say back I am not afraid to leave you, yet I love you,<br />
  You express me better than I can express myself,<br />
  You shall be more to me than my poem.

  I think heroic deeds were all conceiv'd in the open air, and all<br />
<span class='indent' />free poems also,<br />
  I think I could stop here myself and do miracles,<br />
  I think whatever I shall meet on the road I shall like, and whoever<br />
<span class='indent' />beholds me shall like me,<br />
  I think whoever I see must be happy.

<span class='indent' /> 5<br />
  From this hour I ordain myself loos'd of limits and imaginary lines,<br />
  Going where I list, my own master total and absolute,<br />
  Listening to others, considering well what they say,<br />
  Pausing, searching, receiving, contemplating,<br />
  Gently, but with undeniable will, divesting myself of the holds that<br />
<span class='indent' />would hold me.

  I inhale great draughts of space,<br />
  The east and the west are mine, and the north and the south are mine.

  I am larger, better than I thought,<br />
  I did not know I held so much goodness.

  All seems beautiful to me,<br />
  can repeat over to men and women You have done such good to me<br />
<span class='indent' />I would do the same to you,<br />
  I will recruit for myself and you as I go,<br />
  I will scatter myself among men and women as I go,<br />
  I will toss a new gladness and roughness among them,<br />
  Whoever denies me it shall not trouble me,<br />
  Whoever accepts me he or she shall be blessed and shall bless me.

<span class='indent' /> 6<br />
  Now if a thousand perfect men were to appear it would not amaze me,<br />
  Now if a thousand beautiful forms of women appear'd it would not<br />
<span class='indent' />astonish me.

  Now I see the secret of the making of the best persons,<br />
  It is to grow in the open air and to eat and sleep with the earth.

  Here a great personal deed has room,<br />
  (Such a deed seizes upon the hearts of the whole race of men,<br />
  Its effusion of strength and will overwhelms law and mocks all<br />
<span class='indent' />authority and all argument against it.)

  Here is the test of wisdom,<br />
  Wisdom is not finally tested in schools,<br />
  Wisdom cannot be pass'd from one having it to another not having it,<br />
  Wisdom is of the soul, is not susceptible of proof, is its own proof,<br />
  Applies to all stages and objects and qualities and is content,<br />
  Is the certainty of the reality and immortality of things, and the<br />
<span class='indent' />excellence of things;<br />
  Something there is in the float of the sight of things that provokes<br />
<span class='indent' />it out of the soul.

  Now I re-examine philosophies and religions,<br />
  They may prove well in lecture-rooms, yet not prove at all under the<br />
<span class='indent' />spacious clouds and along the landscape and flowing currents.

  Here is realization,<br />
  Here is a man tallied he realizes here what he has in him,<br />
  The past, the future, majesty, love if they are vacant of you, you<br />
<span class='indent' />are vacant of them.

  Only the kernel of every object nourishes;<br />
  Where is he who tears off the husks for you and me?<br />
  Where is he that undoes stratagems and envelopes for you and me?

  Here is adhesiveness, it is not previously fashion'd, it is apropos;<br />
  Do you know what it is as you pass to be loved by strangers?<br />
  Do you know the talk of those turning eye-balls?

<span class='indent' /> 7<br />
  Here is the efflux of the soul,<br />
  The efflux of the soul comes from within through embower'd gates,<br />
<span class='indent' />ever provoking questions,<br />
  These yearnings why are they? these thoughts in the darkness why are they?<br />
  Why are there men and women that while they are nigh me the sunlight<br />
<span class='indent' />expands my blood?<br />
  Why when they leave me do my pennants of joy sink flat and lank?<br />
  Why are there trees I never walk under but large and melodious<br />
<span class='indent' />thoughts descend upon me?<br />
  (I think they hang there winter and summer on those trees and always<br />
<span class='indent' />drop fruit as I pass;)<br />
  What is it I interchange so suddenly with strangers?<br />
  What with some driver as I ride on the seat by his side?<br />
  What with some fisherman drawing his seine by the shore as I walk by<br />
<span class='indent' />and pause?<br />
  What gives me to be free to a woman's and man's good-will? what<br />
<span class='indent' />gives them to be free to mine?

<span class='indent' /> 8<br />
  The efflux of the soul is happiness, here is happiness,<br />
  I think it pervades the open air, waiting at all times,<br />
  Now it flows unto us, we are rightly charged.

  Here rises the fluid and attaching character,<br />
  The fluid and attaching character is the freshness and sweetness of<br />
<span class='indent' />man and woman,<br />
  (The herbs of the morning sprout no fresher and sweeter every day<br />
<span class='indent' />out of the roots of themselves, than it sprouts fresh and sweet<br />
<span class='indent' />continually out of itself.)

  Toward the fluid and attaching character exudes the sweat of the<br />
<span class='indent' />love of young and old,<br />
  From it falls distill'd the charm that mocks beauty and attainments,<br />
  Toward it heaves the shuddering longing ache of contact.

<span class='indent' /> 9<br />
  Allons! whoever you are come travel with me!<br />
  Traveling with me you find what never tires.

  The earth never tires,<br />
  The earth is rude, silent, incomprehensible at first, Nature is rude<br />
<span class='indent' />and incomprehensible at first,<br />
  Be not discouraged, keep on, there are divine things well envelop'd,<br />
  I swear to you there are divine things more beautiful than words can tell.

  Allons! we must not stop here,<br />
  However sweet these laid-up stores, however convenient this dwelling<br />
<span class='indent' />we cannot remain here,<br />
  However shelter'd this port and however calm these waters we must<br />
<span class='indent' />not anchor here,<br />
  However welcome the hospitality that surrounds us we are permitted<br />
<span class='indent' />to receive it but a little while.

<span class='indent' /> 10<br />
  Allons! the inducements shall be greater,<br />
  We will sail pathless and wild seas,<br />
  We will go where winds blow, waves dash, and the Yankee clipper<br />
<span class='indent' />speeds by under full sail.

  Allons! with power, liberty, the earth, the elements,<br />
  Health, defiance, gayety, self-esteem, curiosity;<br />
  Allons! from all formules!<br />
  From your formules, O bat-eyed and materialistic priests.

  The stale cadaver blocks up the passage the burial waits no longer.

  Allons! yet take warning!<br />
  He traveling with me needs the best blood, thews, endurance,<br />
  None may come to the trial till he or she bring courage and health,<br />
  Come not here if you have already spent the best of yourself,<br />
  Only those may come who come in sweet and determin'd bodies,<br />
  No diseas'd person, no rum-drinker or venereal taint is permitted here.

  (I and mine do not convince by arguments, similes, rhymes,<br />
  We convince by our presence.)

<span class='indent' /> 11<br />
  Listen! I will be honest with you,<br />
  I do not offer the old smooth prizes, but offer rough new prizes,<br />
  These are the days that must happen to you:<br />
  You shall not heap up what is call'd riches,<br />
  You shall scatter with lavish hand all that you earn or achieve,<br />
  You but arrive at the city to which you were destin'd, you hardly<br />
<span class='indent' />settle yourself to satisfaction before you are call'd by an<br />
<span class='indent' />irresistible call to depart,<br />
  You shall be treated to the ironical smiles and mockings of those<br />
<span class='indent' />who remain behind you,<br />
  What beckonings of love you receive you shall only answer with<br />
<span class='indent' />passionate kisses of parting,<br />
  You shall not allow the hold of those who spread their reach'd hands<br />
<span class='indent' />toward you.

<span class='indent' /> 12<br />
  Allons! after the great Companions, and to belong to them!<br />
  They too are on the road they are the swift and majestic men they<br />
<span class='indent' />are the greatest women,<br />
  Enjoyers of calms of seas and storms of seas,<br />
  Sailors of many a ship, walkers of many a mile of land,<br />
  Habitues of many distant countries, habitues of far-distant dwellings,<br />
  Trusters of men and women, observers of cities, solitary toilers,<br />
  Pausers and contemplators of tufts, blossoms, shells of the shore,<br />
  Dancers at wedding-dances, kissers of brides, tender helpers of<br />
<span class='indent' />children, bearers of children,<br />
  Soldiers of revolts, standers by gaping graves, lowerers-down of coffins,<br />
  Journeyers over consecutive seasons, over the years, the curious<br />
<span class='indent' />years each emerging from that which preceded it,<br />
  Journeyers as with companions, namely their own diverse phases,<br />
  Forth-steppers from the latent unrealized baby-days,<br />
  Journeyers gayly with their own youth, journeyers with their bearded<br />
<span class='indent' />and well-grain'd manhood,<br />
  Journeyers with their womanhood, ample, unsurpass'd, content,<br />
  Journeyers with their own sublime old age of manhood or womanhood,<br />
  Old age, calm, expanded, broad with the haughty breadth of the universe,<br />
  Old age, flowing free with the delicious near-by freedom of death.

<span class='indent' /> 13<br />
  Allons! to that which is endless as it was beginningless,<br />
  To undergo much, tramps of days, rests of nights,<br />
  To merge all in the travel they tend to, and the days and nights<br />
<span class='indent' />they tend to,<br />
  Again to merge them in the start of superior journeys,<br />
  To see nothing anywhere but what you may reach it and pass it,<br />
  To conceive no time, however distant, but what you may reach it and pass it,<br />
  To look up or down no road but it stretches and waits for you,<br />
<span class='indent' />however long but it stretches and waits for you,<br />
  To see no being, not God's or any, but you also go thither,<br />
  To see no possession but you may possess it, enjoying all without<br />
<span class='indent' />labor or purchase, abstracting the feast yet not abstracting one<br />
<span class='indent' />particle of it,<br />
  To take the best of the farmer's farm and the rich man's elegant<br />
<span class='indent' />villa, and the chaste blessings of the well-married couple, and<br />
<span class='indent' />the fruits of orchards and flowers of gardens,<br />
  To take to your use out of the compact cities as you pass through,<br />
  To carry buildings and streets with you afterward wherever you go,<br />
  To gather the minds of men out of their brains as you encounter<br />
<span class='indent' />them, to gather the love out of their hearts,<br />
  To take your lovers on the road with you, for all that you leave<br />
<span class='indent' />them behind you,<br />
  To know the universe itself as a road, as many roads, as roads for<br />
<span class='indent' />traveling souls.

  All parts away for the progress of souls,<br />
  All religion, all solid things, arts, governments all that was or is<br />
<span class='indent' />apparent upon this globe or any globe, falls into niches and corners<br />
<span class='indent' />before the procession of souls along the grand roads of the universe.

  Of the progress of the souls of men and women along the grand roads of<br />
<span class='indent' />the universe, all other progress is the needed emblem and sustenance.

  Forever alive, forever forward,<br />
  Stately, solemn, sad, withdrawn, baffled, mad, turbulent, feeble,<br />
<span class='indent' />dissatisfied,<br />
  Desperate, proud, fond, sick, accepted by men, rejected by men,<br />
  They go! they go! I know that they go, but I know not where they go,<br />
  But I know that they go toward the best toward something great.

  Whoever you are, come forth! or man or woman come forth!<br />
  You must not stay sleeping and dallying there in the house, though<br />
<span class='indent' />you built it, or though it has been built for you.

  Out of the dark confinement! out from behind the screen!<br />
  It is useless to protest, I know all and expose it.

  Behold through you as bad as the rest,<br />
  Through the laughter, dancing, dining, supping, of people,<br />
  Inside of dresses and ornaments, inside of those wash'd and trimm'd faces,<br />
  Behold a secret silent loathing and despair.

  No husband, no wife, no friend, trusted to hear the confession,<br />
  Another self, a duplicate of every one, skulking and hiding it goes,<br />
  Formless and wordless through the streets of the cities, polite and<br />
<span class='indent' />bland in the parlors,<br />
  In the cars of railroads, in steamboats, in the public assembly,<br />
  Home to the houses of men and women, at the table, in the bedroom,<br />
<span class='indent' />everywhere,<br />
  Smartly attired, countenance smiling, form upright, death under the<br />
<span class='indent' />breast-bones, hell under the skull-bones,<br />
  Under the broadcloth and gloves, under the ribbons and artificial flowers,<br />
  Keeping fair with the customs, speaking not a syllable of itself,<br />
  Speaking of any thing else but never of itself.

<span class='indent' /> 14<br />
  Allons! through struggles and wars!<br />
  The goal that was named cannot be countermanded.

  Have the past struggles succeeded?<br />
  What has succeeded? yourself? your nation? Nature?<br />
  Now understand me well it is provided in the essence of things that<br />
<span class='indent' />from any fruition of success, no matter what, shall come forth<br />
<span class='indent' />something to make a greater struggle necessary.

  My call is the call of battle, I nourish active rebellion,<br />
  He going with me must go well arm'd,<br />
  He going with me goes often with spare diet, poverty, angry enemies,<br />
<span class='indent' />desertions.

<span class='indent' /> 15<br />
  Allons! the road is before us!<br />
  It is safe I have tried it my own feet have tried it well be not<br />
<span class='indent' />detain'd!<br />
  Let the paper remain on the desk unwritten, and the book on the<br />
<span class='indent' />shelf unopen'd!<br />
  Let the tools remain in the workshop! let the money remain unearn'd!<br />
  Let the school stand! mind not the cry of the teacher!<br />
  Let the preacher preach in his pulpit! let the lawyer plead in the<br />
<span class='indent' />court, and the judge expound the law.

  Camerado, I give you my hand!<br />
  I give you my love more precious than money,<br />
  I give you myself before preaching or law;<br />
  Will you give me yourself? will you come travel with me?<br />
  Shall we stick by each other as long as we live?




<h1>Book VIII</h1>


Crossing Brooklyn Ferry

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  Flood-tide below me! I see you face to face!<br />
  Clouds of the west sun there half an hour high I see you also face<br />
<span class='indent' />to face.

  Crowds of men and women attired in the usual costumes, how curious<br />
<span class='indent' />you are to me!<br />
  On the ferry-boats the hundreds and hundreds that cross, returning<br />
<span class='indent' />home, are more curious to me than you suppose,<br />
  And you that shall cross from shore to shore years hence are more<br />
<span class='indent' />to me, and more in my meditations, than you might suppose.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  The impalpable sustenance of me from all things at all hours of the day,<br />
  The simple, compact, well-join'd scheme, myself disintegrated, every<br />
<span class='indent' />one disintegrated yet part of the scheme,<br />
  The similitudes of the past and those of the future,<br />
  The glories strung like beads on my smallest sights and hearings, on<br />
<span class='indent' />the walk in the street and the passage over the river,<br />
  The current rushing so swiftly and swimming with me far away,<br />
  The others that are to follow me, the ties between me and them,<br />
  The certainty of others, the life, love, sight, hearing of others.

  Others will enter the gates of the ferry and cross from shore to shore,<br />
  Others will watch the run of the flood-tide,<br />
  Others will see the shipping of Manhattan north and west, and the<br />
<span class='indent' />heights of Brooklyn to the south and east,<br />
  Others will see the islands large and small;<br />
  Fifty years hence, others will see them as they cross, the sun half<br />
<span class='indent' />an hour high,<br />
  A hundred years hence, or ever so many hundred years hence, others<br />
<span class='indent' />will see them,<br />
  Will enjoy the sunset, the pouring-in of the flood-tide, the<br />
<span class='indent' />falling-back to the sea of the ebb-tide.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  It avails not, time nor place distance avails not,<br />
  I am with you, you men and women of a generation, or ever so many<br />
<span class='indent' />generations hence,<br />
  Just as you feel when you look on the river and sky, so I felt,<br />
  Just as any of you is one of a living crowd, I was one of a crowd,<br />
  Just as you are refresh'd by the gladness of the river and the<br />
<span class='indent' />bright flow, I was refresh'd,<br />
  Just as you stand and lean on the rail, yet hurry with the swift<br />
<span class='indent' />current, I stood yet was hurried,<br />
  Just as you look on the numberless masts of ships and the<br />
<span class='indent' />thick-stemm'd pipes of steamboats, I look'd.

  I too many and many a time cross'd the river of old,<br />
  Watched the Twelfth-month sea-gulls, saw them high in the air<br />
<span class='indent' />floating with motionless wings, oscillating their bodies,<br />
  Saw how the glistening yellow lit up parts of their bodies and left<br />
<span class='indent' />the rest in strong shadow,<br />
  Saw the slow-wheeling circles and the gradual edging toward the south,<br />
  Saw the reflection of the summer sky in the water,<br />
  Had my eyes dazzled by the shimmering track of beams,<br />
  Look'd at the fine centrifugal spokes of light round the shape of my<br />
<span class='indent' />head in the sunlit water,<br />
  Look'd on the haze on the hills southward and south-westward,<br />
  Look'd on the vapor as it flew in fleeces tinged with violet,<br />
  Look'd toward the lower bay to notice the vessels arriving,<br />
  Saw their approach, saw aboard those that were near me,<br />
  Saw the white sails of schooners and sloops, saw the ships at anchor,<br />
  The sailors at work in the rigging or out astride the spars,<br />
  The round masts, the swinging motion of the hulls, the slender<br />
<span class='indent' />serpentine pennants,<br />
  The large and small steamers in motion, the pilots in their pilothouses,<br />
  The white wake left by the passage, the quick tremulous whirl of the wheels,<br />
  The flags of all nations, the falling of them at sunset,<br />
  The scallop-edged waves in the twilight, the ladled cups, the<br />
<span class='indent' />frolic-some crests and glistening,<br />
  The stretch afar growing dimmer and dimmer, the gray walls of the<br />
<span class='indent' />granite storehouses by the docks,<br />
  On the river the shadowy group, the big steam-tug closely flank'd on<br />
<span class='indent' />each side by the barges, the hay-boat, the belated lighter,<br />
  On the neighboring shore the fires from the foundry chimneys burning<br />
<span class='indent' />high and glaringly into the night,<br />
  Casting their flicker of black contrasted with wild red and yellow<br />
<span class='indent' />light over the tops of houses, and down into the clefts of streets.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  These and all else were to me the same as they are to you,<br />
  I loved well those cities, loved well the stately and rapid river,<br />
  The men and women I saw were all near to me,<br />
  Others the same others who look back on me because I look'd forward<br />
<span class='indent' />to them,<br />
  (The time will come, though I stop here to-day and to-night.)

<span class='indent' /> 5<br />
  What is it then between us?<br />
  What is the count of the scores or hundreds of years between us?

  Whatever it is, it avails not distance avails not, and place avails not,<br />
  I too lived, Brooklyn of ample hills was mine,<br />
  I too walk'd the streets of Manhattan island, and bathed in the<br />
<span class='indent' />waters around it,<br />
  I too felt the curious abrupt questionings stir within me,<br />
  In the day among crowds of people sometimes they came upon me,<br />
  In my walks home late at night or as I lay in my bed they came upon me,<br />
  I too had been struck from the float forever held in solution,<br />
  I too had receiv'd identity by my body,<br />
  That I was I knew was of my body, and what I should be I knew I<br />
<span class='indent' />should be of my body.

<span class='indent' /> 6<br />
  It is not upon you alone the dark patches fall,<br />
  The dark threw its patches down upon me also,<br />
  The best I had done seem'd to me blank and suspicious,<br />
  My great thoughts as I supposed them, were they not in reality meagre?<br />
  Nor is it you alone who know what it is to be evil,<br />
  I am he who knew what it was to be evil,<br />
  I too knitted the old knot of contrariety,<br />
  Blabb'd, blush'd, resented, lied, stole, grudg'd,<br />
  Had guile, anger, lust, hot wishes I dared not speak,<br />
  Was wayward, vain, greedy, shallow, sly, cowardly, malignant,<br />
  The wolf, the snake, the hog, not wanting in me.<br />
  The cheating look, the frivolous word, the adulterous wish, not wanting,

  Refusals, hates, postponements, meanness, laziness, none of these wanting,<br />
  Was one with the rest, the days and haps of the rest,<br />
  Was call'd by my nighest name by clear loud voices of young men as<br />
<span class='indent' />they saw me approaching or passing,<br />
  Felt their arms on my neck as I stood, or the negligent leaning of<br />
<span class='indent' />their flesh against me as I sat,<br />
  Saw many I loved in the street or ferry-boat or public assembly, yet<br />
<span class='indent' />never told them a word,<br />
  Lived the same life with the rest, the same old laughing, gnawing, sleeping,<br />
  Play'd the part that still looks back on the actor or actress,<br />
  The same old role, the role that is what we make it, as great as we like,<br />
  Or as small as we like, or both great and small.

<span class='indent' /> 7<br />
  Closer yet I approach you,<br />
  What thought you have of me now, I had as much of you I laid in my<br />
<span class='indent' />stores in advance,<br />
  I consider'd long and seriously of you before you were born.

  Who was to know what should come home to me?<br />
  Who knows but I am enjoying this?<br />
  Who knows, for all the distance, but I am as good as looking at you<br />
<span class='indent' />now, for all you cannot see me?

<span class='indent' /> 8<br />
  Ah, what can ever be more stately and admirable to me than<br />
<span class='indent' />mast-hemm'd Manhattan?<br />
  River and sunset and scallop-edg'd waves of flood-tide?<br />
  The sea-gulls oscillating their bodies, the hay-boat in the<br />
<span class='indent' />twilight, and the belated lighter?<br />
  What gods can exceed these that clasp me by the hand, and with voices I<br />
<span class='indent' />love call me promptly and loudly by my nighest name as approach?<br />
  What is more subtle than this which ties me to the woman or man that<br />
<span class='indent' />looks in my face?<br />
  Which fuses me into you now, and pours my meaning into you?

  We understand then do we not?<br />
  What I promis'd without mentioning it, have you not accepted?<br />
  What the study could not teach what the preaching could not<br />
<span class='indent' />accomplish is accomplish'd, is it not?

<span class='indent' /> 9<br />
  Flow on, river! flow with the flood-tide, and ebb with the ebb-tide!<br />
  Frolic on, crested and scallop-edg'd waves!<br />
  Gorgeous clouds of the sunset! drench with your splendor me, or the<br />
<span class='indent' />men and women generations after me!<br />
  Cross from shore to shore, countless crowds of passengers!<br />
  Stand up, tall masts of Mannahatta! stand up, beautiful hills of Brooklyn!<br />
  Throb, baffled and curious brain! throw out questions and answers!<br />
  Suspend here and everywhere, eternal float of solution!<br />
  Gaze, loving and thirsting eyes, in the house or street or public assembly!<br />
  Sound out, voices of young men! loudly and musically call me by my<br />
<span class='indent' />nighest name!<br />
  Live, old life! play the part that looks back on the actor or actress!<br />
  Play the old role, the role that is great or small according as one<br />
<span class='indent' />makes it!<br />
  Consider, you who peruse me, whether I may not in unknown ways be<br />
<span class='indent' />looking upon you;<br />
  Be firm, rail over the river, to support those who lean idly, yet<br />
<span class='indent' />haste with the hasting current;<br />
  Fly on, sea-birds! fly sideways, or wheel in large circles high in the air;<br />
  Receive the summer sky, you water, and faithfully hold it till all<br />
<span class='indent' />downcast eyes have time to take it from you!<br />
  Diverge, fine spokes of light, from the shape of my head, or any<br />
<span class='indent' />one's head, in the sunlit water!<br />
  Come on, ships from the lower bay! pass up or down, white-sail'd<br />
<span class='indent' />schooners, sloops, lighters!<br />
  Flaunt away, flags of all nations! be duly lower'd at sunset!<br />
  Burn high your fires, foundry chimneys! cast black shadows at<br />
<span class='indent' />nightfall! cast red and yellow light over the tops of the houses!<br />
  Appearances, now or henceforth, indicate what you are,<br />
  You necessary film, continue to envelop the soul,<br />
  About my body for me, and your body for you, be hung our divinest aromas,<br />
  Thrive, cities bring your freight, bring your shows, ample and<br />
<span class='indent' />sufficient rivers,<br />
  Expand, being than which none else is perhaps more spiritual,<br />
  Keep your places, objects than which none else is more lasting.

  You have waited, you always wait, you dumb, beautiful ministers,<br />
  We receive you with free sense at last, and are insatiate henceforward,<br />
  Not you any more shall be able to foil us, or withhold yourselves from us,<br />
  We use you, and do not cast you aside we plant you permanently within us,<br />
  We fathom you not we love you there is perfection in you also,<br />
  You furnish your parts toward eternity,<br />
  Great or small, you furnish your parts toward the soul.




<h1>Book IX</h1>


Song of the Answerer

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  Now list to my morning's romanza, I tell the signs of the Answerer,<br />
  To the cities and farms I sing as they spread in the sunshine before me.

  A young man comes to me bearing a message from his brother,<br />
  How shall the young man know the whether and when of his brother?<br />
  Tell him to send me the signs. And I stand before the young man<br />
<span class='indent' />face to face, and take his right hand in my left hand and his<br />
<span class='indent' />left hand in my right hand,<br />
  And I answer for his brother and for men, and I answer for him that<br />
<span class='indent' />answers for all, and send these signs.

  Him all wait for, him all yield up to, his word is decisive and final,<br />
  Him they accept, in him lave, in him perceive themselves as amid light,<br />
  Him they immerse and he immerses them.

  Beautiful women, the haughtiest nations, laws, the landscape,<br />
<span class='indent' />people, animals,<br />
  The profound earth and its attributes and the unquiet ocean, (so<br />
<span class='indent' />tell I my morning's romanza,)<br />
  All enjoyments and properties and money, and whatever money will buy,<br />
  The best farms, others toiling and planting and he unavoidably reaps,<br />
  The noblest and costliest cities, others grading and building and he<br />
<span class='indent' />domiciles there,<br />
  Nothing for any one but what is for him, near and far are for him,<br />
<span class='indent' />the ships in the offing,<br />
  The perpetual shows and marches on land are for him if they are for anybody.

  He puts things in their attitudes,<br />
  He puts to-day out of himself with plasticity and love,<br />
  He places his own times, reminiscences, parents, brothers and<br />
<span class='indent' />sisters, associations, employment, politics, so that the rest<br />
<span class='indent' />never shame them afterward, nor assume to command them.

  He is the Answerer,<br />
  What can be answer'd he answers, and what cannot be answer'd he<br />
<span class='indent' />shows how it cannot be answer'd.

  A man is a summons and challenge,<br />
  (It is vain to skulk do you hear that mocking and laughter? do you<br />
<span class='indent' />hear the ironical echoes?)

  Books, friendships, philosophers, priests, action, pleasure, pride,<br />
<span class='indent' />beat up and down seeking to give satisfaction,<br />
  He indicates the satisfaction, and indicates them that beat up and<br />
<span class='indent' />down also.

  Whichever the sex, whatever the season or place, he may go freshly<br />
<span class='indent' />and gently and safely by day or by night,<br />
  He has the pass-key of hearts, to him the response of the prying of<br />
<span class='indent' />hands on the knobs.

  His welcome is universal, the flow of beauty is not more welcome or<br />
<span class='indent' />universal than he is,<br />
  The person he favors by day or sleeps with at night is blessed.

  Every existence has its idiom, every thing has an idiom and tongue,<br />
  He resolves all tongues into his own and bestows it upon men, and<br />
<span class='indent' />any man translates, and any man translates himself also,<br />
  One part does not counteract another part, he is the joiner, he sees<br />
<span class='indent' />how they join.

  He says indifferently and alike How are you friend? to the President<br />
<span class='indent' />at his levee,<br />
  And he says Good-day my brother, to Cudge that hoes in the sugar-field,<br />
  And both understand him and know that his speech is right.

  He walks with perfect ease in the capitol,<br />
  He walks among the Congress, and one Representative says to another,<br />
<span class='indent' />Here is our equal appearing and new.

  Then the mechanics take him for a mechanic,<br />
  And the soldiers suppose him to be a soldier, and the sailors that<br />
<span class='indent' />he has follow'd the sea,<br />
  And the authors take him for an author, and the artists for an artist,<br />
  And the laborers perceive he could labor with them and love them,<br />
  No matter what the work is, that he is the one to follow it or has<br />
<span class='indent' />follow'd it,<br />
  No matter what the nation, that he might find his brothers and<br />
<span class='indent' />sisters there.

  The English believe he comes of their English stock,<br />
  A Jew to the Jew he seems, a Russ to the Russ, usual and near,<br />
<span class='indent' />removed from none.

  Whoever he looks at in the traveler's coffee-house claims him,<br />
  The Italian or Frenchman is sure, the German is sure, the Spaniard<br />
<span class='indent' />is sure, and the island Cuban is sure,<br />
  The engineer, the deck-hand on the great lakes, or on the Mississippi<br />
<span class='indent' />or St. Lawrence or Sacramento, or Hudson or Paumanok sound, claims him.

  The gentleman of perfect blood acknowledges his perfect blood,<br />
  The insulter, the prostitute, the angry person, the beggar, see<br />
<span class='indent' />themselves in the ways of him, he strangely transmutes them,<br />
  They are not vile any more, they hardly know themselves they are so grown.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  The indications and tally of time,<br />
  Perfect sanity shows the master among philosophs,<br />
  Time, always without break, indicates itself in parts,<br />
  What always indicates the poet is the crowd of the pleasant company<br />
<span class='indent' />of singers, and their words,<br />
  The words of the singers are the hours or minutes of the light or dark,<br />
<span class='indent' />but the words of the maker of poems are the general light and dark,<br />
  The maker of poems settles justice, reality, immortality,<br />
  His insight and power encircle things and the human race,<br />
  He is the glory and extract thus far of things and of the human race.

  The singers do not beget, only the Poet begets,<br />
  The singers are welcom'd, understood, appear often enough, but rare<br />
<span class='indent' />has the day been, likewise the spot, of the birth of the maker<br />
<span class='indent' />of poems, the Answerer,<br />
  (Not every century nor every five centuries has contain'd such a<br />
<span class='indent' />day, for all its names.)

  The singers of successive hours of centuries may have ostensible<br />
<span class='indent' />names, but the name of each of them is one of the singers,<br />
  The name of each is, eye-singer, ear-singer, head-singer,<br />
<span class='indent' />sweet-singer, night-singer, parlor-singer, love-singer,<br />
<span class='indent' />weird-singer, or something else.

  All this time and at all times wait the words of true poems,<br />
  The words of true poems do not merely please,<br />
  The true poets are not followers of beauty but the august masters of beauty;<br />
  The greatness of sons is the exuding of the greatness of mothers<br />
<span class='indent' />and fathers,<br />
  The words of true poems are the tuft and final applause of science.

  Divine instinct, breadth of vision, the law of reason, health,<br />
<span class='indent' />rudeness of body, withdrawnness,<br />
  Gayety, sun-tan, air-sweetness, such are some of the words of poems.

  The sailor and traveler underlie the maker of poems, the Answerer,<br />
  The builder, geometer, chemist, anatomist, phrenologist, artist, all<br />
<span class='indent' />these underlie the maker of poems, the Answerer.

  The words of the true poems give you more than poems,<br />
  They give you to form for yourself poems, religions, politics, war,<br />
<span class='indent' />peace, behavior, histories, essays, daily life, and every thing else,<br />
  They balance ranks, colors, races, creeds, and the sexes,<br />
  They do not seek beauty, they are sought,<br />
  Forever touching them or close upon them follows beauty, longing,<br />
<span class='indent' />fain, love-sick.

  They prepare for death, yet are they not the finish, but rather the outset,<br />
  They bring none to his or her terminus or to be content and full,<br />
  Whom they take they take into space to behold the birth of stars, to<br />
<span class='indent' />learn one of the meanings,<br />
  To launch off with absolute faith, to sweep through the ceaseless<br />
<span class='indent' />rings and never be quiet again.




<h1>Book X</h1>


Our Old Feuillage

  Always our old feuillage!<br />
  Always Florida's green peninsula always the priceless delta of<br />
<span class='indent' />Louisiana always the cotton-fields of Alabama and Texas,<br />
  Always California's golden hills and hollows, and the silver<br />
<span class='indent' />mountains of New Mexico always soft-breath'd Cuba,<br />
  Always the vast slope drain'd by the Southern sea, inseparable with<br />
<span class='indent' />the slopes drain'd by the Eastern and Western seas,<br />
  The area the eighty-third year of these States, the three and a half<br />
<span class='indent' />millions of square miles,<br />
  The eighteen thousand miles of sea-coast and bay-coast on the main,<br />
<span class='indent' />the thirty thousand miles of river navigation,<br />
  The seven millions of distinct families and the same number of dwellings <br />
<span class='indent' />always these, and more, branching forth into numberless branches,<br />
  Always the free range and diversity always the continent of Democracy;<br />
  Always the prairies, pastures, forests, vast cities, travelers,<br />
<span class='indent' />Kanada, the snows;<br />
  Always these compact lands tied at the hips with the belt stringing<br />
<span class='indent' />the huge oval lakes;<br />
  Always the West with strong native persons, the increasing density there,<br />
<span class='indent' />the habitans, friendly, threatening, ironical, scorning invaders;<br />
  All sights, South, North, East all deeds, promiscuously done at all times,<br />
  All characters, movements, growths, a few noticed, myriads unnoticed,<br />
  Through Mannahatta's streets I walking, these things gathering,<br />
  On interior rivers by night in the glare of pine knots, steamboats<br />
<span class='indent' />wooding up,<br />
  Sunlight by day on the valley of the Susquehanna, and on the valleys<br />
<span class='indent' />of the Potomac and Rappahannock, and the valleys of the Roanoke<br />
<span class='indent' />and Delaware,<br />
  In their northerly wilds beasts of prey haunting the Adirondacks the<br />
<span class='indent' />hills, or lapping the Saginaw waters to drink,<br />
  In a lonesome inlet a sheldrake lost from the flock, sitting on the<br />
<span class='indent' />water rocking silently,<br />
  In farmers' barns oxen in the stable, their harvest labor done, they<br />
<span class='indent' />rest standing, they are too tired,<br />
  Afar on arctic ice the she-walrus lying drowsily while her cubs play around,<br />
  The hawk sailing where men have not yet sail'd, the farthest polar<br />
<span class='indent' />sea, ripply, crystalline, open, beyond the floes,<br />
  White drift spooning ahead where the ship in the tempest dashes,<br />
  On solid land what is done in cities as the bells strike midnight together,<br />
  In primitive woods the sounds there also sounding, the howl of the<br />
<span class='indent' />wolf, the scream of the panther, and the hoarse bellow of the elk,<br />
  In winter beneath the hard blue ice of Moosehead lake, in summer<br />
<span class='indent' />visible through the clear waters, the great trout swimming,<br />
  In lower latitudes in warmer air in the Carolinas the large black<br />
<span class='indent' />buzzard floating slowly high beyond the tree tops,<br />
  Below, the red cedar festoon'd with tylandria, the pines and<br />
<span class='indent' />cypresses growing out of the white sand that spreads far and flat,<br />
  Rude boats descending the big Pedee, climbing plants, parasites with<br />
<span class='indent' />color'd flowers and berries enveloping huge trees,<br />
  The waving drapery on the live-oak trailing long and low,<br />
<span class='indent' />noiselessly waved by the wind,<br />
  The camp of Georgia wagoners just after dark, the supper-fires and<br />
<span class='indent' />the cooking and eating by whites and negroes,<br />
  Thirty or forty great wagons, the mules, cattle, horses, feeding<br />
<span class='indent' />from troughs,<br />
  The shadows, gleams, up under the leaves of the old sycamore-trees,<br />
<span class='indent' />the flames with the black smoke from the pitch-pine curling and rising;<br />
  Southern fishermen fishing, the sounds and inlets of North<br />
<span class='indent' />Carolina's coast, the shad-fishery and the herring-fishery, the<br />
<span class='indent' />large sweep-seines, the windlasses on shore work'd by horses, the<br />
<span class='indent' />clearing, curing, and packing-houses;<br />
  Deep in the forest in piney woods turpentine dropping from the<br />
<span class='indent' />incisions in the trees, there are the turpentine works,<br />
  There are the negroes at work in good health, the ground in all<br />
<span class='indent' />directions is cover'd with pine straw;<br />
  In Tennessee and Kentucky slaves busy in the coalings, at the forge,<br />
<span class='indent' />by the furnace-blaze, or at the corn-shucking,<br />
  In Virginia, the planter's son returning after a long absence,<br />
<span class='indent' />joyfully welcom'd and kiss'd by the aged mulatto nurse,<br />
  On rivers boatmen safely moor'd at nightfall in their boats under<br />
<span class='indent' />shelter of high banks,<br />
  Some of the younger men dance to the sound of the banjo or fiddle,<br />
<span class='indent' />others sit on the gunwale smoking and talking;<br />
  Late in the afternoon the mocking-bird, the American mimic, singing<br />
<span class='indent' />in the Great Dismal Swamp,<br />
  There are the greenish waters, the resinous odor, the plenteous<br />
<span class='indent' />moss, the cypress-tree, and the juniper-tree;<br />
  Northward, young men of Mannahatta, the target company from an<br />
<span class='indent' />excursion returning home at evening, the musket-muzzles all<br />
<span class='indent' />bear bunches of flowers presented by women;<br />
  Children at play, or on his father's lap a young boy fallen asleep,<br />
<span class='indent' />(how his lips move! how he smiles in his sleep!)<br />
  The scout riding on horseback over the plains west of the<br />
<span class='indent' />Mississippi, he ascends a knoll and sweeps his eyes around;<br />
  California life, the miner, bearded, dress'd in his rude costume,<br />
<span class='indent' />the stanch California friendship, the sweet air, the graves one<br />
<span class='indent' />in passing meets solitary just aside the horse-path;<br />
  Down in Texas the cotton-field, the negro-cabins, drivers driving<br />
<span class='indent' />mules or oxen before rude carts, cotton bales piled on banks<br />
<span class='indent' />and wharves;<br />
  Encircling all, vast-darting up and wide, the American Soul, with<br />
<span class='indent' />equal hemispheres, one Love, one Dilation or Pride;<br />
  In arriere the peace-talk with the Iroquois the aborigines, the<br />
<span class='indent' />calumet, the pipe of good-will, arbitration, and indorsement,<br />
  The sachem blowing the smoke first toward the sun and then toward<br />
<span class='indent' />the earth,<br />
  The drama of the scalp-dance enacted with painted faces and guttural<br />
<span class='indent' />exclamations,<br />
  The setting out of the war-party, the long and stealthy march,<br />
  The single file, the swinging hatchets, the surprise and slaughter<br />
<span class='indent' />of enemies;<br />
  All the acts, scenes, ways, persons, attitudes of these States,<br />
<span class='indent' />reminiscences, institutions,<br />
  All these States compact, every square mile of these States without<br />
<span class='indent' />excepting a particle;<br />
  Me pleas'd, rambling in lanes and country fields, Paumanok's fields,<br />
  Observing the spiral flight of two little yellow butterflies<br />
<span class='indent' />shuffling between each other, ascending high in the air,<br />
  The darting swallow, the destroyer of insects, the fall traveler<br />
<span class='indent' />southward but returning northward early in the spring,<br />
  The country boy at the close of the day driving the herd of cows and<br />
<span class='indent' />shouting to them as they loiter to browse by the roadside,<br />
  The city wharf, Boston, Philadelphia, Baltimore, Charleston, New<br />
<span class='indent' />Orleans, San Francisco,<br />
  The departing ships when the sailors heave at the capstan;<br />
  Evening me in my room the setting sun,<br />
  The setting summer sun shining in my open window, showing the<br />
<span class='indent' />swarm of flies, suspended, balancing in the air in the centre<br />
<span class='indent' />of the room, darting athwart, up and down, casting swift<br />
<span class='indent' />shadows in specks on the opposite wall where the shine is;<br />
  The athletic American matron speaking in public to crowds of listeners,<br />
  Males, females, immigrants, combinations, the copiousness, the<br />
<span class='indent' />individuality of the States, each for itself the moneymakers,<br />
  Factories, machinery, the mechanical forces, the windlass, lever,<br />
<span class='indent' />pulley, all certainties,<br />
  The certainty of space, increase, freedom, futurity,<br />
  In space the sporades, the scatter'd islands, the stars on the firm<br />
<span class='indent' />earth, the lands, my lands,<br />
  O lands! all so dear to me what you are, (whatever it is,) I putting it<br />
<span class='indent' />at random in these songs, become a part of that, whatever it is,<br />
  Southward there, I screaming, with wings slow flapping, with the<br />
<span class='indent' />myriads of gulls wintering along the coasts of Florida,<br />
  Otherways there atwixt the banks of the Arkansaw, the Rio Grande,<br />
<span class='indent' />the Nueces, the Brazos, the Tombigbee, the Red River, the<br />
<span class='indent' />Saskatchawan or the Osage, I with the spring waters laughing<br />
<span class='indent' />and skipping and running,<br />
  Northward, on the sands, on some shallow bay of Paumanok, I with<br />
<span class='indent' />parties of snowy herons wading in the wet to seek worms and<br />
<span class='indent' />aquatic plants,<br />
  Retreating, triumphantly twittering, the king-bird, from piercing<br />
<span class='indent' />the crow with its bill, for amusement and I triumphantly twittering,<br />
  The migrating flock of wild geese alighting in autumn to refresh<br />
<span class='indent' />themselves, the body of the flock feed, the sentinels outside<br />
<span class='indent' />move around with erect heads watching, and are from time to time<br />
<span class='indent' />reliev'd by other sentinels and I feeding and taking turns<br />
<span class='indent' />with the rest,<br />
  In Kanadian forests the moose, large as an ox, corner'd by hunters,<br />
<span class='indent' />rising desperately on his hind-feet, and plunging with his<br />
<span class='indent' />fore-feet, the hoofs as sharp as knives and I, plunging at the<br />
<span class='indent' />hunters, corner'd and desperate,<br />
  In the Mannahatta, streets, piers, shipping, store-houses, and the<br />
<span class='indent' />countless workmen working in the shops,<br />
  And I too of the Mannahatta, singing thereof and no less in myself<br />
<span class='indent' />than the whole of the Mannahatta in itself,<br />
  Singing the song of These, my ever-united lands my body no more<br />
<span class='indent' />inevitably united, part to part, and made out of a thousand<br />
<span class='indent' />diverse contributions one identity, any more than my lands<br />
<span class='indent' />are inevitably united and made ONE IDENTITY;<br />
  Nativities, climates, the grass of the great pastoral Plains,<br />
  Cities, labors, death, animals, products, war, good and evil these me,<br />
  These affording, in all their particulars, the old feuillage to me<br />
<span class='indent' />and to America, how can I do less than pass the clew of the union<br />
<span class='indent' />of them, to afford the like to you?<br />
  Whoever you are! how can I but offer you divine leaves, that you<br />
<span class='indent' />also be eligible as I am?<br />
  How can I but as here chanting, invite you for yourself to collect<br />
<span class='indent' />bouquets of the incomparable feuillage of these States?




<h1>Book XI</h1>


A Song of Joys

  O to make the most jubilant song!<br />
  Full of music full of manhood, womanhood, infancy!<br />
  Full of common employments full of grain and trees.

  O for the voices of animals O for the swiftness and balance of fishes!<br />
  O for the dropping of raindrops in a song!<br />
  O for the sunshine and motion of waves in a song!

  O the joy of my spirit it is uncaged it darts like lightning!<br />
  It is not enough to have this globe or a certain time,<br />
  I will have thousands of globes and all time.

  O the engineer's joys! to go with a locomotive!<br />
  To hear the hiss of steam, the merry shriek, the steam-whistle, the<br />
<span class='indent' />laughing locomotive!<br />
  To push with resistless way and speed off in the distance.

  O the gleesome saunter over fields and hillsides!<br />
  The leaves and flowers of the commonest weeds, the moist fresh<br />
<span class='indent' />stillness of the woods,<br />
  The exquisite smell of the earth at daybreak, and all through the forenoon.

  O the horseman's and horsewoman's joys!<br />
  The saddle, the gallop, the pressure upon the seat, the cool<br />
<span class='indent' />gurgling by the ears and hair.

  O the fireman's joys!<br />
  I hear the alarm at dead of night,<br />
  I hear bells, shouts! I pass the crowd, I run!<br />
  The sight of the flames maddens me with pleasure.

  O the joy of the strong-brawn'd fighter, towering in the arena in<br />
<span class='indent' />perfect condition, conscious of power, thirsting to meet his opponent.

  O the joy of that vast elemental sympathy which only the human soul is<br />
<span class='indent' />capable of generating and emitting in steady and limitless floods.

  O the mother's joys!<br />
  The watching, the endurance, the precious love, the anguish, the<br />
<span class='indent' />patiently yielded life.

  O the of increase, growth, recuperation,<br />
  The joy of soothing and pacifying, the joy of concord and harmony.

  O to go back to the place where I was born,<br />
  To hear the birds sing once more,<br />
  To ramble about the house and barn and over the fields once more,<br />
  And through the orchard and along the old lanes once more.

  O to have been brought up on bays, lagoons, creeks, or along the coast,<br />
  To continue and be employ'd there all my life,<br />
  The briny and damp smell, the shore, the salt weeds exposed at low water,<br />
  The work of fishermen, the work of the eel-fisher and clam-fisher;<br />
  I come with my clam-rake and spade, I come with my eel-spear,<br />
  Is the tide out? I Join the group of clam-diggers on the flats,<br />
  I laugh and work with them, I joke at my work like a mettlesome young man;<br />
  In winter I take my eel-basket and eel-spear and travel out on foot<br />
<span class='indent' />on the ice I have a small axe to cut holes in the ice,<br />
  Behold me well-clothed going gayly or returning in the afternoon,<br />
<span class='indent' />my brood of tough boys accompanying me,<br />
  My brood of grown and part-grown boys, who love to be with no<br />
<span class='indent' />one else so well as they love to be with me,<br />
  By day to work with me, and by night to sleep with me.

  Another time in warm weather out in a boat, to lift the lobster-pots<br />
<span class='indent' />where they are sunk with heavy stones, (I know the buoys,)<br />
  O the sweetness of the Fifth-month morning upon the water as I row<br />
<span class='indent' />just before sunrise toward the buoys,<br />
  I pull the wicker pots up slantingly, the dark green lobsters are<br />
<span class='indent' />desperate with their claws as I take them out, I insert<br />
<span class='indent' />wooden pegs in the 'oints of their pincers,

  I go to all the places one after another, and then row back to the shore,<br />
  There in a huge kettle of boiling water the lobsters shall be boil'd<br />
<span class='indent' />till their color becomes scarlet.

  Another time mackerel-taking,<br />
  Voracious, mad for the hook, near the surface, they seem to fill the<br />
<span class='indent' />water for miles;<br />
  Another time fishing for rock-fish in Chesapeake bay, I one of the<br />
<span class='indent' />brown-faced crew;<br />
  Another time trailing for blue-fish off Paumanok, I stand with braced body,<br />
  My left foot is on the gunwale, my right arm throws far out the<br />
<span class='indent' />coils of slender rope,<br />
  In sight around me the quick veering and darting of fifty skiffs, my<br />
<span class='indent' />companions.

  O boating on the rivers,<br />
  The voyage down the St. Lawrence, the superb scenery, the steamers,<br />
  The ships sailing, the Thousand Islands, the occasional timber-raft<br />
<span class='indent' />and the raftsmen with long-reaching sweep-oars,<br />
  The little huts on the rafts, and the stream of smoke when they cook<br />
<span class='indent' />supper at evening.

  (O something pernicious and dread!<br />
  Something far away from a puny and pious life!<br />
  Something unproved! something in a trance!<br />
  Something escaped from the anchorage and driving free.)

  O to work in mines, or forging iron,<br />
  Foundry casting, the foundry itself, the rude high roof, the ample<br />
<span class='indent' />and shadow'd space,<br />
  The furnace, the hot liquid pour'd out and running.

  O to resume the joys of the soldier!<br />
  To feel the presence of a brave commanding officer to feel his sympathy!<br />
  To behold his calmness to be warm'd in the rays of his smile!<br />
  To go to battle to hear the bugles play and the drums beat!<br />
  To hear the crash of artillery to see the glittering of the bayonets<br />
<span class='indent' />and musket-barrels in the sun!

  To see men fall and die and not complain!<br />
  To taste the savage taste of blood to be so devilish!<br />
  To gloat so over the wounds and deaths of the enemy.

  O the whaleman's joys! O I cruise my old cruise again!<br />
  I feel the ship's motion under me, I feel the Atlantic breezes fanning me,<br />
  I hear the cry again sent down from the mast-head, There she blows!<br />
  Again I spring up the rigging to look with the rest we descend,<br />
<span class='indent' />wild with excitement,<br />
  I leap in the lower'd boat, we row toward our prey where he lies,<br />
  We approach stealthy and silent, I see the mountainous mass,<br />
<span class='indent' />lethargic, basking,<br />
  I see the harpooneer standing up, I see the weapon dart from his<br />
<span class='indent' />vigorous arm;<br />
  O swift again far out in the ocean the wounded whale, settling,<br />
<span class='indent' />running to windward, tows me,<br />
  Again I see him rise to breathe, we row close again,<br />
  I see a lance driven through his side, press'd deep, turn'd in the wound,<br />
  Again we back off, I see him settle again, the life is leaving him fast,<br />
  As he rises he spouts blood, I see him swim in circles narrower and<br />
<span class='indent' />narrower, swiftly cutting the water I see him die,<br />
  He gives one convulsive leap in the centre of the circle, and then<br />
<span class='indent' />falls flat and still in the bloody foam.

  O the old manhood of me, my noblest joy of all!<br />
  My children and grand-children, my white hair and beard,<br />
  My largeness, calmness, majesty, out of the long stretch of my life.

  O ripen'd joy of womanhood! O happiness at last!<br />
  I am more than eighty years of age, I am the most venerable mother,<br />
  How clear is my mind how all people draw nigh to me!<br />
  What attractions are these beyond any before? what bloom more<br />
<span class='indent' />than the bloom of youth?<br />
  What beauty is this that descends upon me and rises out of me?

  O the orator's joys!<br />
  To inflate the chest, to roll the thunder of the voice out from the<br />
<span class='indent' />ribs and throat,<br />
  To make the people rage, weep, hate, desire, with yourself,<br />
  To lead America to quell America with a great tongue.

  O the joy of my soul leaning pois'd on itself, receiving identity through<br />
<span class='indent' />materials and loving them, observing characters and absorbing them,<br />
  My soul vibrated back to me from them, from sight, hearing, touch,<br />
<span class='indent' />reason, articulation, comparison, memory, and the like,<br />
  The real life of my senses and flesh transcending my senses and flesh,<br />
  My body done with materials, my sight done with my material eyes,<br />
  Proved to me this day beyond cavil that it is not my material eyes<br />
<span class='indent' />which finally see,<br />
  Nor my material body which finally loves, walks, laughs, shouts,<br />
<span class='indent' />embraces, procreates.

  O the farmer's joys!<br />
  Ohioan's, Illinoisian's, Wisconsinese', Kanadian's, Iowan's,<br />
<span class='indent' />Kansian's, Missourian's, Oregonese' joys!<br />
  To rise at peep of day and pass forth nimbly to work,<br />
  To plough land in the fall for winter-sown crops,<br />
  To plough land in the spring for maize,<br />
  To train orchards, to graft the trees, to gather apples in the fall.

  O to bathe in the swimming-bath, or in a good place along shore,<br />
  To splash the water! to walk ankle-deep, or race naked along the shore.

  O to realize space!<br />
  The plenteousness of all, that there are no bounds,<br />
  To emerge and be of the sky, of the sun and moon and flying<br />
<span class='indent' />clouds, as one with them.

  O the joy a manly self-hood!<br />
  To be servile to none, to defer to none, not to any tyrant known or unknown,<br />
  To walk with erect carriage, a step springy and elastic,<br />
  To look with calm gaze or with a flashing eye,<br />
  To speak with a full and sonorous voice out of a broad chest,<br />
  To confront with your personality all the other personalities of the earth.

  Knowist thou the excellent joys of youth?<br />
  Joys of the dear companions and of the merry word and laughing face?<br />
  Joy of the glad light-beaming day, joy of the wide-breath'd games?<br />
  Joy of sweet music, joy of the lighted ball-room and the dancers?<br />
  Joy of the plenteous dinner, strong carouse and drinking?

  Yet O my soul supreme!<br />
  Knowist thou the joys of pensive thought?<br />
  Joys of the free and lonesome heart, the tender, gloomy heart?<br />
  Joys of the solitary walk, the spirit bow'd yet proud, the suffering<br />
<span class='indent' />and the struggle?<br />
  The agonistic throes, the ecstasies, joys of the solemn musings day<br />
<span class='indent' />or night?<br />
  Joys of the thought of Death, the great spheres Time and Space?<br />
  Prophetic joys of better, loftier love's ideals, the divine wife,<br />
<span class='indent' />the sweet, eternal, perfect comrade?<br />
  Joys all thine own undying one, joys worthy thee O soul.

  O while I live to be the ruler of life, not a slave,<br />
  To meet life as a powerful conqueror,<br />
  No fumes, no ennui, no more complaints or scornful criticisms,<br />
  To these proud laws of the air, the water and the ground, proving<br />
<span class='indent' />my interior soul impregnable,<br />
  And nothing exterior shall ever take command of me.

  For not life's joys alone I sing, repeating the joy of death!<br />
  The beautiful touch of Death, soothing and benumbing a few moments,<br />
<span class='indent' />for reasons,<br />
  Myself discharging my excrementitious body to be burn'd, or render'd<br />
<span class='indent' />to powder, or buried,<br />
  My real body doubtless left to me for other spheres,<br />
  My voided body nothing more to me, returning to the purifications,<br />
<span class='indent' />further offices, eternal uses of the earth.

  O to attract by more than attraction!<br />
  How it is I know not yet behold! the something which obeys none<br />
<span class='indent' />of the rest,<br />
  It is offensive, never defensive yet how magnetic it draws.

  O to struggle against great odds, to meet enemies undaunted!<br />
  To be entirely alone with them, to find how much one can stand!<br />
  To look strife, torture, prison, popular odium, face to face!<br />
  To mount the scaffold, to advance to the muzzles of guns with<br />
<span class='indent' />perfect nonchalance!<br />
  To be indeed a God!

  O to sail to sea in a ship!<br />
  To leave this steady unendurable land,<br />
  To leave the tiresome sameness of the streets, the sidewalks and the<br />
<span class='indent' />houses,<br />
  To leave you O you solid motionless land, and entering a ship,<br />
  To sail and sail and sail!

  O to have life henceforth a poem of new joys!<br />
  To dance, clap hands, exult, shout, skip, leap, roll on, float on!<br />
  To be a sailor of the world bound for all ports,<br />
  A ship itself, (see indeed these sails I spread to the sun and air,)<br />
  A swift and swelling ship full of rich words, full of joys.




<h1>Book XII</h1>


Song of the Broad-Axe

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  Weapon shapely, naked, wan,<br />
  Head from the mother's bowels drawn,<br />
  Wooded flesh and metal bone, limb only one and lip only one,<br />
  Gray-blue leaf by red-heat grown, helve produced from a little seed sown,<br />
  Resting the grass amid and upon,<br />
  To be lean'd and to lean on.

  Strong shapes and attributes of strong shapes, masculine trades,<br />
<span class='indent' />sights and sounds.<br />
  Long varied train of an emblem, dabs of music,<br />
  Fingers of the organist skipping staccato over the keys of the great organ.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  Welcome are all earth's lands, each for its kind,<br />
  Welcome are lands of pine and oak,<br />
  Welcome are lands of the lemon and fig,<br />
  Welcome are lands of gold,<br />
  Welcome are lands of wheat and maize, welcome those of the grape,<br />
  Welcome are lands of sugar and rice,<br />
  Welcome the cotton-lands, welcome those of the white potato and<br />
<span class='indent' />sweet potato,<br />
  Welcome are mountains, flats, sands, forests, prairies,<br />
  Welcome the rich borders of rivers, table-lands, openings,<br />
  Welcome the measureless grazing-lands, welcome the teeming soil of<br />
<span class='indent' />orchards, flax, honey, hemp;<br />
  Welcome just as much the other more hard-faced lands,<br />
  Lands rich as lands of gold or wheat and fruit lands,<br />
  Lands of mines, lands of the manly and rugged ores,<br />
  Lands of coal, copper, lead, tin, zinc,<br />
  Lands of iron lands of the make of the axe.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  The log at the wood-pile, the axe supported by it,<br />
  The sylvan hut, the vine over the doorway, the space clear'd for garden,<br />
  The irregular tapping of rain down on the leaves after the storm is lull'd,<br />
  The walling and moaning at intervals, the thought of the sea,<br />
  The thought of ships struck in the storm and put on their beam ends,<br />
<span class='indent' />and the cutting away of masts,<br />
  The sentiment of the huge timbers of old-fashion'd houses and barns,<br />
  The remember'd print or narrative, the voyage at a venture of men,<br />
<span class='indent' />families, goods,<br />
  The disembarkation, the founding of a new city,<br />
  The voyage of those who sought a New England and found it, the outset<br />
<span class='indent' />anywhere,<br />
  The settlements of the Arkansas, Colorado, Ottawa, Willamette,<br />
  The slow progress, the scant fare, the axe, rifle, saddle-bags;<br />
  The beauty of all adventurous and daring persons,<br />
  The beauty of wood-boys and wood-men with their clear untrimm'd faces,<br />
  The beauty of independence, departure, actions that rely on themselves,<br />
  The American contempt for statutes and ceremonies, the boundless<br />
<span class='indent' />impatience of restraint,<br />
  The loose drift of character, the inkling through random types, the<br />
<span class='indent' />solidification;<br />
  The butcher in the slaughter-house, the hands aboard schooners and<br />
<span class='indent' />sloops, the raftsman, the pioneer,<br />
  Lumbermen in their winter camp, daybreak in the woods, stripes of<br />
<span class='indent' />snow on the limbs of trees, the occasional snapping,<br />
  The glad clear sound of one's own voice, the merry song, the natural<br />
<span class='indent' />life of the woods, the strong day's work,<br />
  The blazing fire at night, the sweet taste of supper, the talk, the<br />
<span class='indent' />bed of hemlock-boughs and the bear-skin;<br />
  The house-builder at work in cities or anywhere,<br />
  The preparatory jointing, squaring, sawing, mortising,<br />
  The hoist-up of beams, the push of them in their places, laying them<br />
<span class='indent' />regular,<br />
  Setting the studs by their tenons in the mortises according as they<br />
<span class='indent' />were prepared,<br />
  The blows of mallets and hammers, the attitudes of the men, their<br />
<span class='indent' />curv'd limbs,<br />
  Bending, standing, astride the beams, driving in pins, holding on by<br />
<span class='indent' />posts and braces,<br />
  The hook'd arm over the plate, the other arm wielding the axe,<br />
  The floor-men forcing the planks close to be nail'd,<br />
  Their postures bringing their weapons downward on the bearers,<br />
  The echoes resounding through the vacant building:<br />
  The huge storehouse carried up in the city well under way,<br />
  The six framing-men, two in the middle and two at each end, carefully<br />
<span class='indent' />bearing on their shoulders a heavy stick for a cross-beam,<br />
  The crowded line of masons with trowels in their right hands rapidly<br />
<span class='indent' />laying the long side-wall, two hundred feet from front to rear,<br />
  The flexible rise and fall of backs, the continual click of the<br />
<span class='indent' />trowels striking the bricks,<br />
  The bricks one after another each laid so workmanlike in its place,<br />
<span class='indent' />and set with a knock of the trowel-handle,<br />
  The piles of materials, the mortar on the mortar-boards, and the<br />
<span class='indent' />steady replenishing by the hod-men;<br />
  Spar-makers in the spar-yard, the swarming row of well-grown apprentices,<br />
  The swing of their axes on the square-hew'd log shaping it toward<br />
<span class='indent' />the shape of a mast,<br />
  The brisk short crackle of the steel driven slantingly into the pine,<br />
  The butter-color'd chips flying off in great flakes and slivers,<br />
  The limber motion of brawny young arms and hips in easy costumes,<br />
  The constructor of wharves, bridges, piers, bulk-heads, floats,<br />
<span class='indent' />stays against the sea;<br />
  The city fireman, the fire that suddenly bursts forth in the<br />
<span class='indent' />close-pack'd square,<br />
  The arriving engines, the hoarse shouts, the nimble stepping and daring,<br />
  The strong command through the fire-trumpets, the falling in line,<br />
<span class='indent' />the rise and fall of the arms forcing the water,<br />
  The slender, spasmic, blue-white jets, the bringing to bear of the<br />
<span class='indent' />hooks and ladders and their execution,<br />
  The crash and cut away of connecting wood-work, or through floors<br />
<span class='indent' />if the fire smoulders under them,<br />
  The crowd with their lit faces watching, the glare and dense shadows;<br />
  The forger at his forge-furnace and the user of iron after him,<br />
  The maker of the axe large and small, and the welder and temperer,<br />
  The chooser breathing his breath on the cold steel and trying the<br />
<span class='indent' />edge with his thumb,<br />
  The one who clean-shapes the handle and sets it firmly in the socket;<br />
  The shadowy processions of the portraits of the past users also,<br />
  The primal patient mechanics, the architects and engineers,<br />
  The far-off Assyrian edifice and Mizra edifice,<br />
  The Roman lictors preceding the consuls,<br />
  The antique European warrior with his axe in combat,<br />
  The uplifted arm, the clatter of blows on the helmeted head,<br />
  The death-howl, the limpsy tumbling body, the rush of friend and foe<br />
<span class='indent' />thither,<br />
  The siege of revolted lieges determin'd for liberty,<br />
  The summons to surrender, the battering at castle gates, the truce<br />
<span class='indent' />and parley,<br />
  The sack of an old city in its time,<br />
  The bursting in of mercenaries and bigots tumultuously and disorderly,<br />
  Roar, flames, blood, drunkenness, madness,<br />
  Goods freely rifled from houses and temples, screams of women in the<br />
<span class='indent' />gripe of brigands,<br />
  Craft and thievery of camp-followers, men running, old persons despairing,<br />
  The hell of war, the cruelties of creeds,<br />
  The list of all executive deeds and words just or unjust,<br />
  The power of personality just or unjust.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  Muscle and pluck forever!<br />
  What invigorates life invigorates death,<br />
  And the dead advance as much as the living advance,<br />
  And the future is no more uncertain than the present,<br />
  For the roughness of the earth and of man encloses as much as the<br />
<span class='indent' />delicatesse of the earth and of man,<br />
  And nothing endures but personal qualities.

  What do you think endures?<br />
  Do you think a great city endures?<br />
  Or a teeming manufacturing state? or a prepared constitution? or the<br />
<span class='indent' />best built steamships?<br />
  Or hotels of granite and iron? or any chef-d'oeuvres of engineering,<br />
<span class='indent' />forts, armaments?

  Away! these are not to be cherish'd for themselves,<br />
  They fill their hour, the dancers dance, the musicians play for them,<br />
  The show passes, all does well enough of course,<br />
  All does very well till one flash of defiance.

  A great city is that which has the greatest men and women,<br />
  If it be a few ragged huts it is still the greatest city in the<br />
<span class='indent' />whole world.

<span class='indent' /> 5<br />
  The place where a great city stands is not the place of stretch'd<br />
<span class='indent' />wharves, docks, manufactures, deposits of produce merely,<br />
  Nor the place of ceaseless salutes of new-comers or the<br />
<span class='indent' />anchor-lifters of the departing,<br />
  Nor the place of the tallest and costliest buildings or shops<br />
<span class='indent' />selling goods from the rest of the earth,<br />
  Nor the place of the best libraries and schools, nor the place where<br />
<span class='indent' />money is plentiest,<br />
  Nor the place of the most numerous population.

  Where the city stands with the brawniest breed of orators and bards,<br />
  Where the city stands that is belov'd by these, and loves them in<br />
<span class='indent' />return and understands them,<br />
  Where no monuments exist to heroes but in the common words and deeds,<br />
  Where thrift is in its place, and prudence is in its place,<br />
  Where the men and women think lightly of the laws,<br />
  Where the slave ceases, and the master of slaves ceases,<br />
  Where the populace rise at once against the never-ending audacity of<br />
<span class='indent' />elected persons,<br />
  Where fierce men and women pour forth as the sea to the whistle of<br />
<span class='indent' />death pours its sweeping and unript waves,<br />
  Where outside authority enters always after the precedence of inside<br />
<span class='indent' />authority,<br />
  Where the citizen is always the head and ideal, and President,<br />
<span class='indent' />Mayor, Governor and what not, are agents for pay,<br />
  Where children are taught to be laws to themselves, and to depend on<br />
<span class='indent' />themselves,<br />
  Where equanimity is illustrated in affairs,<br />
  Where speculations on the soul are encouraged,<br />
  Where women walk in public processions in the streets the same as the men,<br />
  Where they enter the public assembly and take places the same as the men;<br />
  Where the city of the faithfulest friends stands,<br />
  Where the city of the cleanliness of the sexes stands,<br />
  Where the city of the healthiest fathers stands,<br />
  Where the city of the best-bodied mothers stands,<br />
  There the great city stands.

<span class='indent' /> 6<br />
  How beggarly appear arguments before a defiant deed!<br />
  How the floridness of the materials of cities shrivels before a<br />
<span class='indent' />man's or woman's look!

  All waits or goes by default till a strong being appears;<br />
  A strong being is the proof of the race and of the ability of the universe,<br />
  When he or she appears materials are overaw'd,<br />
  The dispute on the soul stops,<br />
  The old customs and phrases are confronted, turn'd back, or laid away.

  What is your money-making now? what can it do now?<br />
  What is your respectability now?<br />
  What are your theology, tuition, society, traditions, statute-books, now?<br />
  Where are your jibes of being now?<br />
  Where are your cavils about the soul now?

<span class='indent' /> 7<br />
  A sterile landscape covers the ore, there is as good as the best for<br />
<span class='indent' />all the forbidding appearance,<br />
  There is the mine, there are the miners,<br />
  The forge-furnace is there, the melt is accomplish'd, the hammersmen<br />
<span class='indent' />are at hand with their tongs and hammers,<br />
  What always served and always serves is at hand.

  Than this nothing has better served, it has served all,<br />
  Served the fluent-tongued and subtle-sensed Greek, and long ere the Greek,<br />
  Served in building the buildings that last longer than any,<br />
  Served the Hebrew, the Persian, the most ancient Hindustanee,<br />
  Served the mound-raiser on the Mississippi, served those whose<br />
<span class='indent' />relics remain in Central America,<br />
  Served Albic temples in woods or on plains, with unhewn pillars and<br />
<span class='indent' />the druids,<br />
  Served the artificial clefts, vast, high, silent, on the<br />
<span class='indent' />snow-cover'd hills of Scandinavia,<br />
  Served those who time out of mind made on the granite walls rough<br />
<span class='indent' />sketches of the sun, moon, stars, ships, ocean waves,<br />
  Served the paths of the irruptions of the Goths, served the pastoral<br />
<span class='indent' />tribes and nomads,<br />
  Served the long distant Kelt, served the hardy pirates of the Baltic,<br />
  Served before any of those the venerable and harmless men of Ethiopia,<br />
  Served the making of helms for the galleys of pleasure and the<br />
<span class='indent' />making of those for war,<br />
  Served all great works on land and all great works on the sea,<br />
  For the mediaeval ages and before the mediaeval ages,<br />
  Served not the living only then as now, but served the dead.

<span class='indent' /> 8<br />
  I see the European headsman,<br />
  He stands mask'd, clothed in red, with huge legs and strong naked arms,<br />
  And leans on a ponderous axe.

  (Whom have you slaughter'd lately European headsman?<br />
  Whose is that blood upon you so wet and sticky?)

  I see the clear sunsets of the martyrs,<br />
  I see from the scaffolds the descending ghosts,<br />
  Ghosts of dead lords, uncrown'd ladies, impeach'd ministers, rejected kings,<br />
  Rivals, traitors, poisoners, disgraced chieftains and the rest.

  I see those who in any land have died for the good cause,<br />
  The seed is spare, nevertheless the crop shall never run out,<br />
  (Mind you O foreign kings, O priests, the crop shall never run out.)
