  I see the blood wash'd entirely away from the axe,<br />
  Both blade and helve are clean,<br />
  They spirt no more the blood of European nobles, they clasp no more<br />
<span class='indent' />the necks of queens.

  I see the headsman withdraw and become useless,<br />
  I see the scaffold untrodden and mouldy, I see no longer any axe upon it,

  I see the mighty and friendly emblem of the power of my own race,<br />
<span class='indent' />the newest, largest race.

<span class='indent' /> 9<br />
  (America! I do not vaunt my love for you,<br />
  I have what I have.)

  The axe leaps!<br />
  The solid forest gives fluid utterances,<br />
  They tumble forth, they rise and form,<br />
  Hut, tent, landing, survey,<br />
  Flail, plough, pick, crowbar, spade,<br />
  Shingle, rail, prop, wainscot, lamb, lath, panel, gable,<br />
  Citadel, ceiling, saloon, academy, organ, exhibition-house, library,<br />
  Cornice, trellis, pilaster, balcony, window, turret, porch,<br />
  Hoe, rake, pitchfork, pencil, wagon, staff, saw, jack-plane, mallet,<br />
<span class='indent' />wedge, rounce,<br />
  Chair, tub, hoop, table, wicket, vane, sash, floor,<br />
  Work-box, chest, string'd instrument, boat, frame, and what not,<br />
  Capitols of States, and capitol of the nation of States,<br />
  Long stately rows in avenues, hospitals for orphans or for the poor or sick,<br />
  Manhattan steamboats and clippers taking the measure of all seas.

  The shapes arise!<br />
  Shapes of the using of axes anyhow, and the users and all that<br />
<span class='indent' />neighbors them,<br />
  Cutters down of wood and haulers of it to the Penobscot or Kenebec,<br />
  Dwellers in cabins among the Californian mountains or by the little<br />
<span class='indent' />lakes, or on the Columbia,<br />
  Dwellers south on the banks of the Gila or Rio Grande, friendly<br />
<span class='indent' />gatherings, the characters and fun,<br />
  Dwellers along the St. Lawrence, or north in Kanada, or down by the<br />
<span class='indent' />Yellowstone, dwellers on coasts and off coasts,<br />
  Seal-fishers, whalers, arctic seamen breaking passages through the ice.

  The shapes arise!<br />
  Shapes of factories, arsenals, foundries, markets,<br />
  Shapes of the two-threaded tracks of railroads,<br />
  Shapes of the sleepers of bridges, vast frameworks, girders, arches,<br />
  Shapes of the fleets of barges, tows, lake and canal craft, river craft,<br />
  Ship-yards and dry-docks along the Eastern and Western seas, and in<br />
<span class='indent' />many a bay and by-place,<br />
  The live-oak kelsons, the pine planks, the spars, the<br />
<span class='indent' />hackmatack-roots for knees,<br />
  The ships themselves on their ways, the tiers of scaffolds, the<br />
<span class='indent' />workmen busy outside and inside,<br />
  The tools lying around, the great auger and little auger, the adze,<br />
<span class='indent' />bolt, line, square, gouge, and bead-plane.

<span class='indent' /> 10<br />
  The shapes arise!<br />
  The shape measur'd, saw'd, jack'd, join'd, stain'd,<br />
  The coffin-shape for the dead to lie within in his shroud,<br />
  The shape got out in posts, in the bedstead posts, in the posts of<br />
<span class='indent' />the bride's bed,<br />
  The shape of the little trough, the shape of the rockers beneath,<br />
<span class='indent' />the shape of the babe's cradle,<br />
  The shape of the floor-planks, the floor-planks for dancers' feet,<br />
  The shape of the planks of the family home, the home of the friendly<br />
<span class='indent' />parents and children,<br />
  The shape of the roof of the home of the happy young man and<br />
<span class='indent' />woman, the roof over the well-married young man and woman,<br />
  The roof over the supper joyously cook'd by the chaste wife, and joyously<br />
<span class='indent' />eaten by the chaste husband, content after his day's work.

  The shapes arise!<br />
  The shape of the prisoner's place in the court-room, and of him or<br />
<span class='indent' />her seated in the place,<br />
  The shape of the liquor-bar lean'd against by the young rum-drinker<br />
<span class='indent' />and the old rum-drinker,<br />
  The shape of the shamed and angry stairs trod by sneaking foot- steps,<br />
  The shape of the sly settee, and the adulterous unwholesome couple,<br />
  The shape of the gambling-board with its devilish winnings and losings,<br />
  The shape of the step-ladder for the convicted and sentenced<br />
<span class='indent' />murderer, the murderer with haggard face and pinion'd arms,<br />
  The sheriff at hand with his deputies, the silent and white-lipp'd<br />
<span class='indent' />crowd, the dangling of the rope.

  The shapes arise!<br />
  Shapes of doors giving many exits and entrances,<br />
  The door passing the dissever'd friend flush'd and in haste,<br />
  The door that admits good news and bad news,<br />
  The door whence the son left home confident and puff'd up,<br />
  The door he enter'd again from a long and scandalous absence,<br />
<span class='indent' />diseas'd, broken down, without innocence, without means.

<span class='indent' /> 11<br />
  Her shape arises,<br />
  She less guarded than ever, yet more guarded than ever,<br />
  The gross and soil'd she moves among do not make her gross and soil'd,<br />
  She knows the thoughts as she passes, nothing is conceal'd from her,<br />
  She is none the less considerate or friendly therefor,<br />
  She is the best belov'd, it is without exception, she has no reason<br />
<span class='indent' />to fear and she does not fear,<br />
  Oaths, quarrels, hiccupp'd songs, smutty expressions, are idle to<br />
<span class='indent' />her as she passes,<br />
  She is silent, she is possess'd of herself, they do not offend her,<br />
  She receives them as the laws of Nature receive them, she is strong,<br />
  She too is a law of Nature there is no law stronger than she is.

<span class='indent' /> 12<br />
  The main shapes arise!<br />
  Shapes of Democracy total, result of centuries,<br />
  Shapes ever projecting other shapes,<br />
  Shapes of turbulent manly cities,<br />
  Shapes of the friends and home-givers of the whole earth,<br />
  Shapes bracing the earth and braced with the whole earth.




<h1>Book XIII</h1>


Song of the Exposition

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  (Ah little recks the laborer,<br />
  How near his work is holding him to God,<br />
  The loving Laborer through space and time.)

  After all not to create only, or found only,<br />
  But to bring perhaps from afar what is already founded,<br />
  To give it our own identity, average, limitless, free,<br />
  To fill the gross the torpid bulk with vital religious fire,<br />
  Not to repel or destroy so much as accept, fuse, rehabilitate,<br />
  To obey as well as command, to follow more than to lead,<br />
  These also are the lessons of our New World;<br />
  While how little the New after all, how much the Old, Old World!

  Long and long has the grass been growing,<br />
  Long and long has the rain been falling,<br />
  Long has the globe been rolling round.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  Come Muse migrate from Greece and Ionia,<br />
  Cross out please those immensely overpaid accounts,<br />
  That matter of Troy and Achilles' wrath, and AEneas', Odysseus' wanderings,<br />
  Placard "Removed" and "To Let" on the rocks of your snowy Parnassus,<br />
  Repeat at Jerusalem, place the notice high on jaffa's gate and on<br />
<span class='indent' />Mount Moriah,<br />
  The same on the walls of your German, French and Spanish castles,<br />
<span class='indent' />and Italian collections,<br />
  For know a better, fresher, busier sphere, a wide, untried domain<br />
<span class='indent' />awaits, demands you.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  Responsive to our summons,<br />
  Or rather to her long-nurs'd inclination,<br />
  Join'd with an irresistible, natural gravitation,<br />
  She comes! I hear the rustling of her gown,<br />
  I scent the odor of her breath's delicious fragrance,<br />
  I mark her step divine, her curious eyes a-turning, rolling,<br />
  Upon this very scene.

  The dame of dames! can I believe then,<br />
  Those ancient temples, sculptures classic, could none of them retain her?<br />
  Nor shades of Virgil and Dante, nor myriad memories, poems, old<br />
<span class='indent' />associations, magnetize and hold on to her?<br />
  But that she's left them all and here?

  Yes, if you will allow me to say so,<br />
  I, my friends, if you do not, can plainly see her,<br />
  The same undying soul of earth's, activity's, beauty's, heroism's<br />
<span class='indent' />expression,<br />
  Out from her evolutions hither come, ended the strata of her former themes,<br />
  Hidden and cover'd by to-day's, foundation of to-day's,<br />
  Ended, deceas'd through time, her voice by Castaly's fountain,<br />
  Silent the broken-lipp'd Sphynx in Egypt, silent all those century-<br />
<span class='indent' />baffling tombs,<br />
  Ended for aye the epics of Asia's, Europe's helmeted warriors, ended<br />
<span class='indent' />the primitive call of the muses,<br />
  Calliope's call forever closed, Clio, Melpomene, Thalia dead,<br />
  Ended the stately rhythmus of Una and Oriana, ended the quest of the<br />
<span class='indent' />holy Graal,<br />
  Jerusalem a handful of ashes blown by the wind, extinct,<br />
  The Crusaders' streams of shadowy midnight troops sped with the sunrise,<br />
  Amadis, Tancred, utterly gone, Charlemagne, Roland, Oliver gone,<br />
  Palmerin, ogre, departed, vanish'd the turrets that Usk from its<br />
<span class='indent' />waters reflected,<br />
  Arthur vanish'd with all his knights, Merlin and Lancelot and<br />
<span class='indent' />Galahad, all gone, dissolv'd utterly like an exhalation;<br />
  Pass'd! pass'd! for us, forever pass'd, that once so mighty world,<br />
<span class='indent' />now void, inanimate, phantom world,<br />
  Embroider'd, dazzling, foreign world, with all its gorgeous legends, myths,<br />
  Its kings and castles proud, its priests and warlike lords and<br />
<span class='indent' />courtly dames,<br />
  Pass'd to its charnel vault, coffin'd with crown and armor on,<br />
  Blazon'd with Shakspere's purple page,<br />
  And dirged by Tennyson's sweet sad rhyme.

  I say I see, my friends, if you do not, the illustrious emigre, (having it<br />
<span class='indent' />is true in her day, although the same, changed, journey'd considerable,)<br />
  Making directly for this rendezvous, vigorously clearing a path for<br />
<span class='indent' />herself, striding through the confusion,<br />
  By thud of machinery and shrill steam-whistle undismay'd,<br />
  Bluff'd not a bit by drain-pipe, gasometers, artificial fertilizers,<br />
  Smiling and pleas'd with palpable intent to stay,<br />
  She's here, install'd amid the kitchen ware!

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  But hold don't I forget my manners?<br />
  To introduce the stranger, (what else indeed do I live to chant<br />
<span class='indent' />for?) to thee Columbia;<br />
  In liberty's name welcome immortal! clasp hands,<br />
  And ever henceforth sisters dear be both.

  Fear not O Muse! truly new ways and days receive, surround you,<br />
  I candidly confess a queer, queer race, of novel fashion,<br />
  And yet the same old human race, the same within, without,<br />
  Faces and hearts the same, feelings the same, yearnings the same,<br />
  The same old love, beauty and use the same.

<span class='indent' /> 5<br />
  We do not blame thee elder World, nor really separate ourselves from thee,<br />
  (Would the son separate himself from the father?)<br />
  Looking back on thee, seeing thee to thy duties, grandeurs, through<br />
<span class='indent' />past ages bending, building,<br />
  We build to ours to-day.

  Mightier than Egypt's tombs,<br />
  Fairer than Grecia's, Roma's temples,<br />
  Prouder than Milan's statued, spired cathedral,<br />
  More picturesque than Rhenish castle-keeps,<br />
  We plan even now to raise, beyond them all,<br />
  Thy great cathedral sacred industry, no tomb,<br />
  A keep for life for practical invention.

  As in a waking vision,<br />
  E'en while I chant I see it rise, I scan and prophesy outside and in,<br />
  Its manifold ensemble.

  Around a palace, loftier, fairer, ampler than any yet,<br />
  Earth's modern wonder, history's seven outstripping,<br />
  High rising tier on tier with glass and iron facades,<br />
  Gladdening the sun and sky, enhued in cheerfulest hues,<br />
  Bronze, lilac, robin's-egg, marine and crimson,<br />
  Over whose golden roof shall flaunt, beneath thy banner Freedom,<br />
  The banners of the States and flags of every land,<br />
  A brood of lofty, fair, but lesser palaces shall cluster.

  Somewhere within their walls shall all that forwards perfect human<br />
<span class='indent' />life be started,<br />
  Tried, taught, advanced, visibly exhibited.

  Not only all the world of works, trade, products,<br />
  But all the workmen of the world here to be represented.

  Here shall you trace in flowing operation,<br />
  In every state of practical, busy movement, the rills of civilization,<br />
  Materials here under your eye shall change their shape as if by magic,<br />
  The cotton shall be pick'd almost in the very field,<br />
  Shall be dried, clean'd, ginn'd, baled, spun into thread and cloth<br />
<span class='indent' />before you,<br />
  You shall see hands at work at all the old processes and all the new ones,<br />
  You shall see the various grains and how flour is made and then<br />
<span class='indent' />bread baked by the bakers,<br />
  You shall see the crude ores of California and Nevada passing on and<br />
<span class='indent' />on till they become bullion,<br />
  You shall watch how the printer sets type, and learn what a<br />
<span class='indent' />composing-stick is,<br />
  You shall mark in amazement the Hoe press whirling its cylinders,<br />
<span class='indent' />shedding the printed leaves steady and fast,<br />
  The photograph, model, watch, pin, nail, shall be created before you.

  In large calm halls, a stately museum shall teach you the infinite<br />
<span class='indent' />lessons of minerals,<br />
  In another, woods, plants, vegetation shall be illustrated in<br />
<span class='indent' />another animals, animal life and development.

  One stately house shall be the music house,<br />
  Others for other arts learning, the sciences, shall all be here,<br />
  None shall be slighted, none but shall here be honor'd, help'd, exampled.

<span class='indent' /> 6<br />
  (This, this and these, America, shall be your pyramids and obelisks,<br />
  Your Alexandrian Pharos, gardens of Babylon,<br />
  Your temple at Olympia.)

  The male and female many laboring not,<br />
  Shall ever here confront the laboring many,<br />
  With precious benefits to both, glory to all,<br />
  To thee America, and thee eternal Muse.

  And here shall ye inhabit powerful Matrons!<br />
  In your vast state vaster than all the old,<br />
  Echoed through long, long centuries to come,<br />
  To sound of different, prouder songs, with stronger themes,<br />
  Practical, peaceful life, the people's life, the People themselves,<br />
  Lifted, illumin'd, bathed in peace elate, secure in peace.

<span class='indent' /> 7<br />
  Away with themes of war! away with war itself!<br />
  Hence from my shuddering sight to never more return that show of<br />
<span class='indent' />blacken'd, mutilated corpses!<br />
  That hell unpent and raid of blood, fit for wild tigers or for<br />
<span class='indent' />lop-tongued wolves, not reasoning men,<br />
  And in its stead speed industry's campaigns,<br />
  With thy undaunted armies, engineering,<br />
  Thy pennants labor, loosen'd to the breeze,<br />
  Thy bugles sounding loud and clear.

  Away with old romance!<br />
  Away with novels, plots and plays of foreign courts,<br />
  Away with love-verses sugar'd in rhyme, the intrigues, amours of idlers,<br />
  Fitted for only banquets of the night where dancers to late music slide,<br />
  The unhealthy pleasures, extravagant dissipations of the few,<br />
  With perfumes, heat and wine, beneath the dazzling chandeliers.

  To you ye reverent sane sisters,<br />
  I raise a voice for far superber themes for poets and for art,<br />
  To exalt the present and the real,<br />
  To teach the average man the glory of his daily walk and trade,<br />
  To sing in songs how exercise and chemical life are never to be baffled,<br />
  To manual work for each and all, to plough, hoe, dig,<br />
  To plant and tend the tree, the berry, vegetables, flowers,<br />
  For every man to see to it that he really do something, for every woman too;<br />
  To use the hammer and the saw, (rip, or cross-cut,)<br />
  To cultivate a turn for carpentering, plastering, painting,<br />
  To work as tailor, tailoress, nurse, hostler, porter,<br />
  To invent a little, something ingenious, to aid the washing, cooking,<br />
<span class='indent' />cleaning,<br />
  And hold it no disgrace to take a hand at them themselves.

  I say I bring thee Muse to-day and here,<br />
  All occupations, duties broad and close,<br />
  Toil, healthy toil and sweat, endless, without cessation,<br />
  The old, old practical burdens, interests, joys,<br />
  The family, parentage, childhood, husband and wife,<br />
  The house-comforts, the house itself and all its belongings,<br />
  Food and its preservation, chemistry applied to it,<br />
  Whatever forms the average, strong, complete, sweet-blooded man or<br />
<span class='indent' />woman, the perfect longeve personality,<br />
  And helps its present life to health and happiness, and shapes its soul,<br />
  For the eternal real life to come.

  With latest connections, works, the inter-transportation of the world,<br />
  Steam-power, the great express lines, gas, petroleum,<br />
  These triumphs of our time, the Atlantic's delicate cable,<br />
  The Pacific railroad, the Suez canal, the Mont Cenis and Gothard and<br />
<span class='indent' />Hoosac tunnels, the Brooklyn bridge,<br />
  This earth all spann'd with iron rails, with lines of steamships<br />
<span class='indent' />threading in every sea,<br />
  Our own rondure, the current globe I bring.

<span class='indent' /> 8<br />
  And thou America,<br />
  Thy offspring towering e'er so high, yet higher Thee above all towering,<br />
  With Victory on thy left, and at thy right hand Law;<br />
  Thou Union holding all, fusing, absorbing, tolerating all,<br />
  Thee, ever thee, I sing.

  Thou, also thou, a World,<br />
  With all thy wide geographies, manifold, different, distant,<br />
  Rounded by thee in one one common orbic language,<br />
  One common indivisible destiny for All.

  And by the spells which ye vouchsafe to those your ministers in earnest,<br />
  I here personify and call my themes, to make them pass before ye.

  Behold, America! (and thou, ineffable guest and sister!)<br />
  For thee come trooping up thy waters and thy lands;<br />
  Behold! thy fields and farms, thy far-off woods and mountains,<br />
  As in procession coming.

  Behold, the sea itself,<br />
  And on its limitless, heaving breast, the ships;<br />
  See, where their white sails, bellying in the wind, speckle the<br />
<span class='indent' />green and blue,<br />
  See, the steamers coming and going, steaming in or out of port,<br />
  See, dusky and undulating, the long pennants of smoke.

  Behold, in Oregon, far in the north and west,<br />
  Or in Maine, far in the north and east, thy cheerful axemen,<br />
  Wielding all day their axes.

  Behold, on the lakes, thy pilots at their wheels, thy oarsmen,<br />
  How the ash writhes under those muscular arms!

  There by the furnace, and there by the anvil,<br />
  Behold thy sturdy blacksmiths swinging their sledges,<br />
  Overhand so steady, overhand they turn and fall with joyous clank,<br />
  Like a tumult of laughter.

  Mark the spirit of invention everywhere, thy rapid patents,<br />
  Thy continual workshops, foundries, risen or rising,<br />
  See, from their chimneys how the tall flame-fires stream.

  Mark, thy interminable farms, North, South,<br />
  Thy wealthy daughter-states, Eastern and Western,<br />
  The varied products of Ohio, Pennsylvania, Missouri, Georgia, Texas,<br />
<span class='indent' />and the rest,<br />
  Thy limitless crops, grass, wheat, sugar, oil, corn, rice, hemp, hops,<br />
  Thy barns all fill'd, the endless freight-train and the bulging store-house,<br />
  The grapes that ripen on thy vines, the apples in thy orchards,<br />
  Thy incalculable lumber, beef, pork, potatoes, thy coal, thy gold<br />
<span class='indent' />and silver,<br />
  The inexhaustible iron in thy mines.

  All thine O sacred Union!<br />
  Ships, farms, shops, barns, factories, mines,<br />
  City and State, North, South, item and aggregate,<br />
  We dedicate, dread Mother, all to thee!

  Protectress absolute, thou! bulwark of all!<br />
  For well we know that while thou givest each and all, (generous as God,)<br />
  Without thee neither all nor each, nor land, home,<br />
  Nor ship, nor mine, nor any here this day secure,<br />
  Nor aught, nor any day secure.

<span class='indent' /> 9<br />
  And thou, the Emblem waving over all!<br />
  Delicate beauty, a word to thee, (it may be salutary,)<br />
  Remember thou hast not always been as here to-day so comfortably<br />
<span class='indent' />ensovereign'd,<br />
  In other scenes than these have I observ'd thee flag,<br />
  Not quite so trim and whole and freshly blooming in folds of<br />
<span class='indent' />stainless silk,<br />
  But I have seen thee bunting, to tatters torn upon thy splinter'd staff,<br />
  Or clutch'd to some young color-bearer's breast with desperate hands,<br />
  Savagely struggled for, for life or death, fought over long,<br />
  'Mid cannons' thunder-crash and many a curse and groan and yell, and<br />
<span class='indent' />rifle-volleys cracking sharp,<br />
  And moving masses as wild demons surging, and lives as nothing risk'd,<br />
  For thy mere remnant grimed with dirt and smoke and sopp'd in blood,<br />
  For sake of that, my beauty, and that thou might'st dally as now<br />
<span class='indent' />secure up there,<br />
  Many a good man have I seen go under.

  Now here and these and hence in peace, all thine O Flag!<br />
  And here and hence for thee, O universal Muse! and thou for them!<br />
  And here and hence O Union, all the work and workmen thine!<br />
  None separate from thee henceforth One only, we and thou,<br />
  (For the blood of the children, what is it, only the blood maternal?<br />
  And lives and works, what are they all at last, except the roads to<br />
<span class='indent' />faith and death?)

  While we rehearse our measureless wealth, it is for thee, dear Mother,<br />
  We own it all and several to-day indissoluble in thee;<br />
  Think not our chant, our show, merely for products gross or lucre <br />
<span class='indent' />it is for thee, the soul in thee, electric, spiritual!<br />
  Our farms, inventions, crops, we own in thee! cities and States in thee!<br />
  Our freedom all in thee! our very lives in thee!




<h1>Book XIV</h1>


Song of the Redwood-Tree

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  A California song,<br />
  A prophecy and indirection, a thought impalpable to breathe as air,<br />
  A chorus of dryads, fading, departing, or hamadryads departing,<br />
  A murmuring, fateful, giant voice, out of the earth and sky,<br />
  Voice of a mighty dying tree in the redwood forest dense.

  Farewell my brethren,<br />
  Farewell O earth and sky, farewell ye neighboring waters,<br />
  My time has ended, my term has come.

  Along the northern coast,<br />
  Just back from the rock-bound shore and the caves,<br />
  In the saline air from the sea in the Mendocino country,<br />
  With the surge for base and accompaniment low and hoarse,<br />
  With crackling blows of axes sounding musically driven by strong arms,<br />
  Riven deep by the sharp tongues of the axes, there in the redwood<br />
<span class='indent' />forest dense,<br />
  I heard the might tree its death-chant chanting.

  The choppers heard not, the camp shanties echoed not,<br />
  The quick-ear'd teamsters and chain and jack-screw men heard not,<br />
  As the wood-spirits came from their haunts of a thousand years to<br />
<span class='indent' />join the refrain,<br />
  But in my soul I plainly heard.

  Murmuring out of its myriad leaves,<br />
  Down from its lofty top rising two hundred feet high,<br />
  Out of its stalwart trunk and limbs, out of its foot-thick bark,<br />
  That chant of the seasons and time, chant not of the past only but<br />
<span class='indent' />the future.

  You untold life of me,<br />
  And all you venerable and innocent joys,<br />
  Perennial hardy life of me with joys 'mid rain and many a summer sun,<br />
  And the white snows and night and the wild winds;<br />
  O the great patient rugged joys, my soul's strong joys unreck'd by man,<br />
  (For know I bear the soul befitting me, I too have consciousness, identity,<br />
  And all the rocks and mountains have, and all the earth,)<br />
  Joys of the life befitting me and brothers mine,<br />
  Our time, our term has come.

  Nor yield we mournfully majestic brothers,<br />
  We who have grandly fill'd our time,<br />
  With Nature's calm content, with tacit huge delight,<br />
  We welcome what we wrought for through the past,<br />
  And leave the field for them.

  For them predicted long,<br />
  For a superber race, they too to grandly fill their time,<br />
  For them we abdicate, in them ourselves ye forest kings.'<br />
  In them these skies and airs, these mountain peaks, Shasta, Nevadas,<br />
  These huge precipitous cliffs, this amplitude, these valleys, far Yosemite,<br />
  To be in them absorb'd, assimilated.

  Then to a loftier strain,<br />
  Still prouder, more ecstatic rose the chant,<br />
  As if the heirs, the deities of the West,<br />
  Joining with master-tongue bore part.

  Not wan from Asia's fetiches,<br />
  Nor red from Europe's old dynastic slaughter-house,<br />
  (Area of murder-plots of thrones, with scent left yet of wars and<br />
<span class='indent' />scaffolds everywhere,<br />
  But come from Nature's long and harmless throes, peacefully builded thence,<br />
  These virgin lands, lands of the Western shore,<br />
  To the new culminating man, to you, the empire new,<br />
  You promis'd long, we pledge, we dedicate.

  You occult deep volitions,<br />
  You average spiritual manhood, purpose of all, pois'd on yourself,<br />
<span class='indent' />giving not taking law,<br />
  You womanhood divine, mistress and source of all, whence life and<br />
<span class='indent' />love and aught that comes from life and love,<br />
  You unseen moral essence of all the vast materials of America, age<br />
<span class='indent' />upon age working in death the same as life,)<br />
  You that, sometimes known, oftener unknown, really shape and mould<br />
<span class='indent' />the New World, adjusting it to Time and Space,<br />
  You hidden national will lying in your abysms, conceal'd but ever alert,<br />
  You past and present purposes tenaciously pursued, may-be<br />
<span class='indent' />unconscious of yourselves,<br />
  Unswerv'd by all the passing errors, perturbations of the surface;<br />
  You vital, universal, deathless germs, beneath all creeds, arts,<br />
<span class='indent' />statutes, literatures,<br />
  Here build your homes for good, establish here, these areas entire,<br />
<span class='indent' />lands of the Western shore,<br />
  We pledge, we dedicate to you.

  For man of you, your characteristic race,<br />
  Here may he hardy, sweet, gigantic grow, here tower proportionate to Nature,<br />
  Here climb the vast pure spaces unconfined, uncheck'd by wall or roof,<br />
  Here laugh with storm or sun, here joy, here patiently inure,<br />
  Here heed himself, unfold himself, (not others' formulas heed,)<br />
  here fill his time,<br />
  To duly fall, to aid, unreck'd at last,<br />
  To disappear, to serve.

  Thus on the northern coast,<br />
  In the echo of teamsters' calls and the clinking chains, and the<br />
<span class='indent' />music of choppers' axes,<br />
  The falling trunk and limbs, the crash, the muffled shriek, the groan,<br />
  Such words combined from the redwood-tree, as of voices ecstatic,<br />
<span class='indent' />ancient and rustling,<br />
  The century-lasting, unseen dryads, singing, withdrawing,<br />
  All their recesses of forests and mountains leaving,<br />
  From the Cascade range to the Wahsatch, or Idaho far, or Utah,<br />
  To the deities of the modern henceforth yielding,<br />
  The chorus and indications, the vistas of coming humanity, the<br />
<span class='indent' />settlements, features all,<br />
  In the Mendocino woods I caught.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  The flashing and golden pageant of California,<br />
  The sudden and gorgeous drama, the sunny and ample lands,<br />
  The long and varied stretch from Puget sound to Colorado south,<br />
  Lands bathed in sweeter, rarer, healthier air, valleys and mountain cliffs,<br />
  The fields of Nature long prepared and fallow, the silent, cyclic chemistry,<br />
  The slow and steady ages plodding, the unoccupied surface ripening,<br />
<span class='indent' />the rich ores forming beneath;<br />
  At last the New arriving, assuming, taking possession,<br />
  A swarming and busy race settling and organizing everywhere,<br />
  Ships coming in from the whole round world, and going out to the<br />
<span class='indent' />whole world,<br />
  To India and China and Australia and the thousand island paradises<br />
<span class='indent' />of the Pacific,<br />
  Populous cities, the latest inventions, the steamers on the rivers,<br />
<span class='indent' />the railroads, with many a thrifty farm, with machinery,<br />
  And wool and wheat and the grape, and diggings of yellow gold.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  But more in you than these, lands of the Western shore,<br />
  (These but the means, the implements, the standing-ground,)<br />
  I see in you, certain to come, the promise of thousands of years,<br />
<span class='indent' />till now deferr'd,<br />
  Promis'd to be fulfill'd, our common kind, the race.

  The new society at last, proportionate to Nature,<br />
  In man of you, more than your mountain peaks or stalwart trees imperial,<br />
  In woman more, far more, than all your gold or vines, or even vital air.

  Fresh come, to a new world indeed, yet long prepared,<br />
  I see the genius of the modern, child of the real and ideal,<br />
  Clearing the ground for broad humanity, the true America, heir of<br />
<span class='indent' />the past so grand,<br />
  To build a grander future.




<h1>Book XV</h1>


A Song for Occupations

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  A song for occupations!<br />
  In the labor of engines and trades and the labor of fields I find<br />
<span class='indent' />the developments,<br />
  And find the eternal meanings.

  Workmen and Workwomen!<br />
  Were all educations practical and ornamental well display'd out of<br />
<span class='indent' />me, what would it amount to?<br />
  Were I as the head teacher, charitable proprietor, wise statesman,<br />
<span class='indent' />what would it amount to?<br />
  Were I to you as the boss employing and paying you, would that satisfy you?

  The learn'd, virtuous, benevolent, and the usual terms,<br />
  A man like me and never the usual terms.

  Neither a servant nor a master I,<br />
  I take no sooner a large price than a small price, I will have my<br />
<span class='indent' />own whoever enjoys me,<br />
  I will be even with you and you shall be even with me.

  If you stand at work in a shop I stand as nigh as the nighest in the<br />
<span class='indent' />same shop,<br />
  If you bestow gifts on your brother or dearest friend I demand as<br />
<span class='indent' />good as your brother or dearest friend,<br />
  If your lover, husband, wife, is welcome by day or night, I must be<br />
<span class='indent' />personally as welcome,<br />
  If you become degraded, criminal, ill, then I become so for your sake,<br />
  If you remember your foolish and outlaw'd deeds, do you think I<br />
<span class='indent' />cannot remember my own foolish and outlaw'd deeds?<br />
  If you carouse at the table I carouse at the opposite side of the table,<br />
  If you meet some stranger in the streets and love him or her, why<br />
<span class='indent' />I often meet strangers in the street and love them.

  Why what have you thought of yourself?<br />
  Is it you then that thought yourself less?<br />
  Is it you that thought the President greater than you?<br />
  Or the rich better off than you? or the educated wiser than you?

  (Because you are greasy or pimpled, or were once drunk, or a thief,<br />
  Or that you are diseas'd, or rheumatic, or a prostitute,<br />
  Or from frivolity or impotence, or that you are no scholar and never<br />
<span class='indent' />saw your name in print,<br />
  Do you give in that you are any less immortal?)

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  Souls of men and women! it is not you I call unseen, unheard,<br />
<span class='indent' />untouchable and untouching,<br />
  It is not you I go argue pro and con about, and to settle whether<br />
<span class='indent' />you are alive or no,<br />
  I own publicly who you are, if nobody else owns.

  Grown, half-grown and babe, of this country and every country,<br />
<span class='indent' />in-doors and out-doors, one just as much as the other, I see,<br />
  And all else behind or through them.

  The wife, and she is not one jot less than the husband,<br />
  The daughter, and she is just as good as the son,<br />
  The mother, and she is every bit as much as the father.

  Offspring of ignorant and poor, boys apprenticed to trades,<br />
  Young fellows working on farms and old fellows working on farms,<br />
  Sailor-men, merchant-men, coasters, immigrants,<br />
  All these I see, but nigher and farther the same I see,<br />
  None shall escape me and none shall wish to escape me.

  I bring what you much need yet always have,<br />
  Not money, amours, dress, eating, erudition, but as good,<br />
  I send no agent or medium, offer no representative of value, but<br />
<span class='indent' />offer the value itself.

  There is something that comes to one now and perpetually,<br />
  It is not what is printed, preach'd, discussed, it eludes discussion<br />
<span class='indent' />and print,<br />
  It is not to be put in a book, it is not in this book,<br />
  It is for you whoever you are, it is no farther from you than your<br />
<span class='indent' />hearing and sight are from you,<br />
  It is hinted by nearest, commonest, readiest, it is ever provoked by them.

  You may read in many languages, yet read nothing about it,<br />
  You may read the President's message and read nothing about it there,<br />
  Nothing in the reports from the State department or Treasury<br />
<span class='indent' />department, or in the daily papers or weekly papers,<br />
  Or in the census or revenue returns, prices current, or any accounts<br />
<span class='indent' />of stock.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  The sun and stars that float in the open air,<br />
  The apple-shaped earth and we upon it, surely the drift of them is<br />
<span class='indent' />something grand,<br />
  I do not know what it is except that it is grand, and that it is happiness,<br />
  And that the enclosing purport of us here is not a speculation or<br />
<span class='indent' />bon-mot or reconnoissance,<br />
  And that it is not something which by luck may turn out well for us,<br />
<span class='indent' />and without luck must be a failure for us,<br />
  And not something which may yet be retracted in a certain contingency.

  The light and shade, the curious sense of body and identity, the<br />
<span class='indent' />greed that with perfect complaisance devours all things,<br />
  The endless pride and outstretching of man, unspeakable joys and sorrows,<br />
  The wonder every one sees in every one else he sees, and the wonders<br />
<span class='indent' />that fill each minute of time forever,<br />
  What have you reckon'd them for, camerado?<br />
  Have you reckon'd them for your trade or farm-work? or for the<br />
<span class='indent' />profits of your store?<br />
  Or to achieve yourself a position? or to fill a gentleman's leisure,<br />
<span class='indent' />or a lady's leisure?

  Have you reckon'd that the landscape took substance and form that it<br />
<span class='indent' />might be painted in a picture?<br />
  Or men and women that they might be written of, and songs sung?<br />
  Or the attraction of gravity, and the great laws and harmonious combinations<br />
<span class='indent' />and the fluids of the air, as subjects for the savans?<br />
  Or the brown land and the blue sea for maps and charts?<br />
  Or the stars to be put in constellations and named fancy names?<br />
  Or that the growth of seeds is for agricultural tables, or<br />
<span class='indent' />agriculture itself?

  Old institutions, these arts, libraries, legends, collections, and<br />
<span class='indent' />the practice handed along in manufactures, will we rate them so high?<br />
  Will we rate our cash and business high? I have no objection,<br />
  I rate them as high as the highest then a child born of a woman and<br />
<span class='indent' />man I rate beyond all rate.

  We thought our Union grand, and our Constitution grand,<br />
  I do not say they are not grand and good, for they are,<br />
  I am this day just as much in love with them as you,<br />
  Then I am in love with You, and with all my fellows upon the earth.

  We consider bibles and religions divine I do not say they are not divine,<br />
  I say they have all grown out of you, and may grow out of you still,<br />
  It is not they who give the life, it is you who give the life,<br />
  Leaves are not more shed from the trees, or trees from the earth,<br />
<span class='indent' />than they are shed out of you.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  The sum of all known reverence I add up in you whoever you are,<br />
  The President is there in the White House for you, it is not you who<br />
<span class='indent' />are here for him,<br />
  The Secretaries act in their bureaus for you, not you here for them,<br />
  The Congress convenes every Twelfth-month for you,<br />
  Laws, courts, the forming of States, the charters of cities, the<br />
<span class='indent' />going and coming of commerce and malls, are all for you.

  List close my scholars dear,<br />
  Doctrines, politics and civilization exurge from you,<br />
  Sculpture and monuments and any thing inscribed anywhere are tallied in you,<br />
  The gist of histories and statistics as far back as the records<br />
<span class='indent' />reach is in you this hour, and myths and tales the same,<br />
  If you were not breathing and walking here, where would they all be?<br />
  The most renown'd poems would be ashes, orations and plays would<br />
<span class='indent' />be vacuums.

  All architecture is what you do to it when you look upon it,<br />
  (Did you think it was in the white or gray stone? or the lines of<br />
<span class='indent' />the arches and cornices?)

  All music is what awakes from you when you are reminded by the instruments,<br />
  It is not the violins and the cornets, it is not the oboe nor the<br />
<span class='indent' />beating drums, nor the score of the baritone singer singing his<br />
<span class='indent' />sweet romanza, nor that of the men's chorus, nor that of the<br />
<span class='indent' />women's chorus,<br />
  It is nearer and farther than they.

<span class='indent' /> 5<br />
  Will the whole come back then?<br />
  Can each see signs of the best by a look in the looking-glass? is<br />
<span class='indent' />there nothing greater or more?<br />
  Does all sit there with you, with the mystic unseen soul?

  Strange and hard that paradox true I give,<br />
  Objects gross and the unseen soul are one.

  House-building, measuring, sawing the boards,<br />
  Blacksmithing, glass-blowing, nail-making, coopering, tin-roofing,<br />
<span class='indent' />shingle-dressing,<br />
  Ship-joining, dock-building, fish-curing, flagging of sidewalks by flaggers,<br />
  The pump, the pile-driver, the great derrick, the coal-kiln and brickkiln,<br />
  Coal-mines and all that is down there, the lamps in the darkness,<br />
<span class='indent' />echoes, songs, what meditations, what vast native thoughts<br />
<span class='indent' />looking through smutch'd faces,<br />
  Iron-works, forge-fires in the mountains or by river-banks, men<br />
<span class='indent' />around feeling the melt with huge crowbars, lumps of ore, the<br />
<span class='indent' />due combining of ore, limestone, coal,<br />
  The blast-furnace and the puddling-furnace, the loup-lump at the<br />
<span class='indent' />bottom of the melt at last, the rolling-mill, the stumpy bars<br />
<span class='indent' />of pig-iron, the strong clean-shaped Trail for railroads,<br />
  Oil-works, silk-works, white-lead-works, the sugar-house,<br />
<span class='indent' />steam-saws, the great mills and factories,<br />
  Stone-cutting, shapely trimmings for facades or window or door-lintels,<br />
<span class='indent' />the mallet, the tooth-chisel, the jib to protect the thumb,<br />
  The calking-iron, the kettle of boiling vault-cement, and the fire<br />
<span class='indent' />under the kettle,<br />
  The cotton-bale, the stevedore's hook, the saw and buck of the<br />
<span class='indent' />sawyer, the mould of the moulder, the working-knife of the<br />
<span class='indent' />butcher, the ice-saw, and all the work with ice,<br />
  The work and tools of the rigger, grappler, sail-maker, block-maker,<br />
  Goods of gutta-percha, papier-mache, colors, brushes, brush-making,<br />
<span class='indent' />glazier's implements,<br />
  The veneer and glue-pot, the confectioner's ornaments, the decanter<br />
<span class='indent' />and glasses, the shears and flat-iron,<br />
  The awl and knee-strap, the pint measure and quart measure, the<br />
<span class='indent' />counter and stool, the writing-pen of quill or metal, the making<br />
<span class='indent' />of all sorts of edged tools,<br />
  The brewery, brewing, the malt, the vats, every thing that is done<br />
<span class='indent' />by brewers, wine-makers, vinegar-makers,<br />
  Leather-dressing, coach-making, boiler-making, rope-twisting,<br />
<span class='indent' />distilling, sign-painting, lime-burning, cotton-picking,<br />
<span class='indent' />electroplating, electrotyping, stereotyping,<br />
  Stave-machines, planing-machines, reaping-machines,<br />
<span class='indent' />ploughing-machines, thrashing-machines, steam wagons,<br />
  The cart of the carman, the omnibus, the ponderous dray,<br />
  Pyrotechny, letting off color'd fireworks at night, fancy figures and jets;<br />
  Beef on the butcher's stall, the slaughter-house of the butcher, the<br />
<span class='indent' />butcher in his killing-clothes,<br />
  The pens of live pork, the killing-hammer, the hog-hook, the<br />
<span class='indent' />scalder's tub, gutting, the cutter's cleaver, the packer's maul,<br />
<span class='indent' />and the plenteous winterwork of pork-packing,<br />
  Flour-works, grinding of wheat, rye, maize, rice, the barrels and<br />
<span class='indent' />the half and quarter barrels, the loaded barges, the high piles<br />
<span class='indent' />on wharves and levees,<br />
  The men and the work of the men on ferries, railroads, coasters,<br />
<span class='indent' />fish-boats, canals;<br />
  The hourly routine of your own or any man's life, the shop, yard,<br />
<span class='indent' />store, or factory,<br />
  These shows all near you by day and night workman! whoever you<br />
<span class='indent' />are, your daily life!

  In that and them the heft of the heaviest in that and them far more<br />
<span class='indent' />than you estimated, (and far less also,)<br />
  In them realities for you and me, in them poems for you and me,<br />
  In them, not yourself-you and your soul enclose all things,<br />
<span class='indent' />regardless of estimation,<br />
  In them the development good in them all themes, hints, possibilities.

  I do not affirm that what you see beyond is futile, I do not advise<br />
<span class='indent' />you to stop,<br />
  I do not say leadings you thought great are not great,<br />
  But I say that none lead to greater than these lead to.

<span class='indent' /> 6<br />
  Will you seek afar off? you surely come back at last,<br />
  In things best known to you finding the best, or as good as the best,<br />
  In folks nearest to you finding the sweetest, strongest, lovingest,<br />
  Happiness, knowledge, not in another place but this place, not for<br />
<span class='indent' />another hour but this hour,<br />
  Man in the first you see or touch, always in friend, brother,<br />
<span class='indent' />nighest neighbor woman in mother, sister, wife,<br />
  The popular tastes and employments taking precedence in poems or anywhere,<br />
  You workwomen and workmen of these States having your own divine<br />
<span class='indent' />and strong life,<br />
  And all else giving place to men and women like you.<br />
  When the psalm sings instead of the singer,

  When the script preaches instead of the preacher,<br />
  When the pulpit descends and goes instead of the carver that carved<br />
<span class='indent' />the supporting desk,<br />
  When I can touch the body of books by night or by day, and when they<br />
<span class='indent' />touch my body back again,<br />
  When a university course convinces like a slumbering woman and child<br />
<span class='indent' />convince,<br />
  When the minted gold in the vault smiles like the night-watchman's daughter,<br />
  When warrantee deeds loafe in chairs opposite and are my friendly<br />
<span class='indent' />companions,<br />
  I intend to reach them my hand, and make as much of them as I do<br />
<span class='indent' />of men and women like you.




<h1>Book XVI</h1>


A Song of the Rolling Earth

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  A song of the rolling earth, and of words according,<br />
  Were you thinking that those were the words, those upright lines?<br />
<span class='indent' />those curves, angles, dots?<br />
  No, those are not the words, the substantial words are in the ground<br />
<span class='indent' />and sea,<br />
  They are in the air, they are in you.

  Were you thinking that those were the words, those delicious sounds<br />
<span class='indent' />out of your friends' mouths?<br />
  No, the real words are more delicious than they.

  Human bodies are words, myriads of words,<br />
  (In the best poems re-appears the body, man's or woman's,<br />
<span class='indent' />well-shaped, natural, gay,<br />
  Every part able, active, receptive, without shame or the need of shame.)

  Air, soil, water, fire those are words,<br />
  I myself am a word with them my qualities interpenetrate with<br />
<span class='indent' />theirs my name is nothing to them,<br />
  Though it were told in the three thousand languages, what would<br />
<span class='indent' />air, soil, water, fire, know of my name?

  A healthy presence, a friendly or commanding gesture, are words,<br />
<span class='indent' />sayings, meanings,<br />
  The charms that go with the mere looks of some men and women,<br />
<span class='indent' />are sayings and meanings also.

  The workmanship of souls is by those inaudible words of the earth,<br />
  The masters know the earth's words and use them more than audible words.

  Amelioration is one of the earth's words,<br />
  The earth neither lags nor hastens,<br />
  It has all attributes, growths, effects, latent in itself from the jump,<br />
  It is not half beautiful only, defects and excrescences show just as<br />
<span class='indent' />much as perfections show.

  The earth does not withhold, it is generous enough,<br />
  The truths of the earth continually wait, they are not so conceal'd either,<br />
  They are calm, subtle, untransmissible by print,<br />
  They are imbued through all things conveying themselves willingly,<br />
  Conveying a sentiment and invitation, I utter and utter,<br />
  I speak not, yet if you hear me not of what avail am I to you?<br />
  To bear, to better, lacking these of what avail am I?

  (Accouche! accouchez!<br />
  Will you rot your own fruit in yourself there?<br />
  Will you squat and stifle there?)

  The earth does not argue,<br />
  Is not pathetic, has no arrangements,<br />
  Does not scream, haste, persuade, threaten, promise,<br />
  Makes no discriminations, has no conceivable failures,<br />
  Closes nothing, refuses nothing, shuts none out,<br />
  Of all the powers, objects, states, it notifies, shuts none out.

  The earth does not exhibit itself nor refuse to exhibit itself,<br />
<span class='indent' />possesses still underneath,<br />
  Underneath the ostensible sounds, the august chorus of heroes, the<br />
<span class='indent' />wail of slaves,<br />
  Persuasions of lovers, curses, gasps of the dying, laughter of young<br />
<span class='indent' />people, accents of bargainers,<br />
  Underneath these possessing words that never fall.

  To her children the words of the eloquent dumb great mother never fail,<br />
  The true words do not fail, for motion does not fail and reflection<br />
<span class='indent' />does not fall,<br />
  Also the day and night do not fall, and the voyage we pursue does not fall.

  Of the interminable sisters,<br />
  Of the ceaseless cotillons of sisters,<br />
  Of the centripetal and centrifugal sisters, the elder and younger sisters,<br />
  The beautiful sister we know dances on with the rest.

  With her ample back towards every beholder,<br />
  With the fascinations of youth and the equal fascinations of age,<br />
  Sits she whom I too love like the rest, sits undisturb'd,<br />
  Holding up in her hand what has the character of a mirror, while her<br />
<span class='indent' />eyes glance back from it,<br />
  Glance as she sits, inviting none, denying none,<br />
  Holding a mirror day and night tirelessly before her own face.

  Seen at hand or seen at a distance,<br />
  Duly the twenty-four appear in public every day,<br />
  Duly approach and pass with their companions or a companion,<br />
  Looking from no countenances of their own, but from the countenances<br />
<span class='indent' />of those who are with them,<br />
  From the countenances of children or women or the manly countenance,<br />
  From the open countenances of animals or from inanimate things,<br />
  From the landscape or waters or from the exquisite apparition of the sky,<br />
  From our countenances, mine and yours, faithfully returning them,<br />
  Every day in public appearing without fall, but never twice with the<br />
<span class='indent' />same companions.

  Embracing man, embracing all, proceed the three hundred and<br />
<span class='indent' />sixty-five resistlessly round the sun;<br />
  Embracing all, soothing, supporting, follow close three hundred and<br />
<span class='indent' />sixty-five offsets of the first, sure and necessary as they.

  Tumbling on steadily, nothing dreading,<br />
  Sunshine, storm, cold, heat, forever withstanding, passing, carrying,<br />
  The soul's realization and determination still inheriting,<br />
  The fluid vacuum around and ahead still entering and dividing,<br />
  No balk retarding, no anchor anchoring, on no rock striking,<br />
  Swift, glad, content, unbereav'd, nothing losing,<br />
  Of all able and ready at any time to give strict account,<br />
  The divine ship sails the divine sea.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  Whoever you are! motion and reflection are especially for you,<br />
  The divine ship sails the divine sea for you.

  Whoever you are! you are he or she for whom the earth is solid and liquid,<br />
  You are he or she for whom the sun and moon hang in the sky,<br />
  For none more than you are the present and the past,<br />
  For none more than you is immortality.

  Each man to himself and each woman to herself, is the word of the<br />
<span class='indent' />past and present, and the true word of immortality;<br />
  No one can acquire for another not one,<br />
  Not one can grow for another not one.

  The song is to the singer, and comes back most to him,<br />
  The teaching is to the teacher, and comes back most to him,<br />
  The murder is to the murderer, and comes back most to him,<br />
  The theft is to the thief, and comes back most to him,<br />
  The love is to the lover, and comes back most to him,<br />
  The gift is to the giver, and comes back most to him it cannot fail,<br />
  The oration is to the orator, the acting is to the actor and actress<br />
<span class='indent' />not to the audience,<br />
  And no man understands any greatness or goodness but his own, or<br />
<span class='indent' />the indication of his own.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  I swear the earth shall surely be complete to him or her who shall<br />
<span class='indent' />be complete,<br />
  The earth remains jagged and broken only to him or her who remains<br />
<span class='indent' />jagged and broken.

  I swear there is no greatness or power that does not emulate those<br />
<span class='indent' />of the earth,<br />
  There can be no theory of any account unless it corroborate the<br />
<span class='indent' />theory of the earth,<br />
  No politics, song, religion, behavior, or what not, is of account,<br />
<span class='indent' />unless it compare with the amplitude of the earth,<br />
  Unless it face the exactness, vitality, impartiality, rectitude of<br />
<span class='indent' />the earth.

  I swear I begin to see love with sweeter spasms than that which<br />
<span class='indent' />responds love,<br />
  It is that which contains itself, which never invites and never refuses.

  I swear I begin to see little or nothing in audible words,<br />
  All merges toward the presentation of the unspoken meanings of the earth,<br />
  Toward him who sings the songs of the body and of the truths of the earth,<br />
  Toward him who makes the dictionaries of words that print cannot touch.

  I swear I see what is better than to tell the best,<br />
  It is always to leave the best untold.

  When I undertake to tell the best I find I cannot,<br />
  My tongue is ineffectual on its pivots,<br />
  My breath will not be obedient to its organs,<br />
  I become a dumb man.

  The best of the earth cannot be told anyhow, all or any is best,<br />
  It is not what you anticipated, it is cheaper, easier, nearer,<br />
  Things are not dismiss'd from the places they held before,<br />
  The earth is just as positive and direct as it was before,<br />
  Facts, religions, improvements, politics, trades, are as real as before,<br />
  But the soul is also real, it too is positive and direct,<br />
  No reasoning, no proof has establish'd it,<br />
  Undeniable growth has establish'd it.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  These to echo the tones of souls and the phrases of souls,<br />
  (If they did not echo the phrases of souls what were they then?<br />
  If they had not reference to you in especial what were they then?)

  I swear I will never henceforth have to do with the faith that tells<br />
<span class='indent' />the best,<br />
  I will have to do only with that faith that leaves the best untold.

  Say on, sayers! sing on, singers!<br />
  Delve! mould! pile the words of the earth!<br />
  Work on, age after age, nothing is to be lost,<br />
  It may have to wait long, but it will certainly come in use,<br />
  When the materials are all prepared and ready, the architects shall appear.

  I swear to you the architects shall appear without fall,<br />
  I swear to you they will understand you and justify you,<br />
  The greatest among them shall be he who best knows you, and encloses<br />
<span class='indent' />all and is faithful to all,<br />
  He and the rest shall not forget you, they shall perceive that you<br />
<span class='indent' />are not an iota less than they,<br />
  You shall be fully glorified in them.




Youth, Day, Old Age and Night

  Youth, large, lusty, loving youth full of grace, force, fascination,<br />
  Do you know that Old Age may come after you with equal grace,<br />
<span class='indent' />force, fascination?

  Day full-blown and splendid-day of the immense sun, action,<br />
<span class='indent' />ambition, laughter,<br />
  The Night follows close with millions of suns, and sleep and<br />
<span class='indent' />restoring darkness.




<h1>Book XVII.  Birds Of Passage</h1>


Song of the Universal

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  Come said the Muse,<br />
  Sing me a song no poet yet has chanted,<br />
  Sing me the universal.

  In this broad earth of ours,<br />
  Amid the measureless grossness and the slag,<br />
  Enclosed and safe within its central heart,<br />
  Nestles the seed perfection.

  By every life a share or more or less,<br />
  None born but it is born, conceal'd or unconceal'd the seed is waiting.

<span class='indent' /> 2<br />
  Lo! keen-eyed towering science,<br />
  As from tall peaks the modern overlooking,<br />
  Successive absolute fiats issuing.

  Yet again, lo! the soul, above all science,<br />
  For it has history gather'd like husks around the globe,<br />
  For it the entire star-myriads roll through the sky.

  In spiral routes by long detours,<br />
  (As a much-tacking ship upon the sea,)<br />
  For it the partial to the permanent flowing,<br />
  For it the real to the ideal tends.

  For it the mystic evolution,<br />
  Not the right only justified, what we call evil also justified.

  Forth from their masks, no matter what,<br />
  From the huge festering trunk, from craft and guile and tears,<br />
  Health to emerge and joy, joy universal.

  Out of the bulk, the morbid and the shallow,<br />
  Out of the bad majority, the varied countless frauds of men and states,<br />
  Electric, antiseptic yet, cleaving, suffusing all,<br />
  Only the good is universal.

<span class='indent' /> 3<br />
  Over the mountain-growths disease and sorrow,<br />
  An uncaught bird is ever hovering, hovering,<br />
  High in the purer, happier air.

  From imperfection's murkiest cloud,<br />
  Darts always forth one ray of perfect light,<br />
  One flash of heaven's glory.

  To fashion's, custom's discord,<br />
  To the mad Babel-din, the deafening orgies,<br />
  Soothing each lull a strain is heard, just heard,<br />
  From some far shore the final chorus sounding.

  O the blest eyes, the happy hearts,<br />
  That see, that know the guiding thread so fine,<br />
  Along the mighty labyrinth.

<span class='indent' /> 4<br />
  And thou America,<br />
  For the scheme's culmination, its thought and its reality,<br />
  For these (not for thyself) thou hast arrived.

  Thou too surroundest all,<br />
  Embracing carrying welcoming all, thou too by pathways broad and new,<br />
  To the ideal tendest.

  The measure'd faiths of other lands, the grandeurs of the past,<br />
  Are not for thee, but grandeurs of thine own,<br />
  Deific faiths and amplitudes, absorbing, comprehending all,<br />
  All eligible to all.

  All, all for immortality,<br />
  Love like the light silently wrapping all,<br />
  Nature's amelioration blessing all,<br />
  The blossoms, fruits of ages, orchards divine and certain,<br />
  Forms, objects, growths, humanities, to spiritual images ripening.

  Give me O God to sing that thought,<br />
  Give me, give him or her I love this quenchless faith,<br />
  In Thy ensemble, whatever else withheld withhold not from us,<br />
  Belief in plan of Thee enclosed in Time and Space,<br />
  Health, peace, salvation universal.

  Is it a dream?<br />
  Nay but the lack of it the dream,<br />
  And failing it life's lore and wealth a dream,<br />
  And all the world a dream.




Pioneers! O Pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Come my tan-faced children,<br />
  Follow well in order, get your weapons ready,<br />
  Have you your pistols? have you your sharp-edged axes?<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> For we cannot tarry here,<br />
  We must march my darlings, we must bear the brunt of danger,<br />
  We the youthful sinewy races, all the rest on us depend,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> O you youths, Western youths,<br />
  So impatient, full of action, full of manly pride and friendship,<br />
  Plain I see you Western youths, see you tramping with the foremost,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Have the elder races halted?<br />
  Do they droop and end their lesson, wearied over there beyond the seas?<br />
  We take up the task eternal, and the burden and the lesson,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> All the past we leave behind,<br />
  We debouch upon a newer mightier world, varied world,<br />
  Fresh and strong the world we seize, world of labor and the march,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> We detachments steady throwing,<br />
  Down the edges, through the passes, up the mountains steep,<br />
  Conquering, holding, daring, venturing as we go the unknown ways,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> We primeval forests felling,<br />
  We the rivers stemming, vexing we and piercing deep the mines within,<br />
  We the surface broad surveying, we the virgin soil upheaving,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Colorado men are we,<br />
  From the peaks gigantic, from the great sierras and the high plateaus,<br />
  From the mine and from the gully, from the hunting trail we come,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> From Nebraska, from Arkansas,<br />
  Central inland race are we, from Missouri, with the continental<br />
<span class='indent' /> blood intervein'd,<br />
  All the hands of comrades clasping, all the Southern, all the Northern,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> O resistless restless race!<br />
  O beloved race in all! O my breast aches with tender love for all!<br />
  O I mourn and yet exult, I am rapt with love for all,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Raise the mighty mother mistress,<br />
  Waving high the delicate mistress, over all the starry mistress,<br />
<span class='indent' /> (bend your heads all,)<br />
  Raise the fang'd and warlike mistress, stern, impassive, weapon'd mistress,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> See my children, resolute children,<br />
  By those swarms upon our rear we must never yield or falter,<br />
  Ages back in ghostly millions frowning there behind us urging,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> On and on the compact ranks,<br />
  With accessions ever waiting, with the places of the dead quickly fill'd,<br />
  Through the battle, through defeat, moving yet and never stopping,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> O to die advancing on!<br />
  Are there some of us to droop and die? has the hour come?<br />
  Then upon the march we fittest die, soon and sure the gap is fill'd.<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> All the pulses of the world,<br />
  Falling in they beat for us, with the Western movement beat,<br />
  Holding single or together, steady moving to the front, all for us,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Life's involv'd and varied pageants,<br />
  All the forms and shows, all the workmen at their work,<br />
  All the seamen and the landsmen, all the masters with their slaves,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' />All the hapless silent lovers,<br />
  All the prisoners in the prisons, all the righteous and the wicked,<br />
  All the joyous, all the sorrowing, all the living, all the dying,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' />I too with my soul and body,<br />
  We, a curious trio, picking, wandering on our way,<br />
  Through these shores amid the shadows, with the apparitions pressing,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' />Lo, the darting bowling orb!<br />
  Lo, the brother orbs around, all the clustering suns and planets,<br />
  All the dazzling days, all the mystic nights with dreams,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' />These are of us, they are with us,<br />
  All for primal needed work, while the followers there in embryo wait behind,<br />
  We to-day's procession heading, we the route for travel clearing,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

  O you daughters of the West!<br />
  O you young and elder daughters! O you mothers and you wives!<br />
  Never must you be divided, in our ranks you move united,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Minstrels latent on the prairies!<br />
  (Shrouded bards of other lands, you may rest, you have done your work,)<br />
  Soon I hear you coming warbling, soon you rise and tramp amid us,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Not for delectations sweet,<br />
  Not the cushion and the slipper, not the peaceful and the studious,<br />
  Not the riches safe and palling, not for us the tame enjoyment,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Do the feasters gluttonous feast?<br />
  Do the corpulent sleepers sleep? have they lock'd and bolted doors?<br />
  Still be ours the diet hard, and the blanket on the ground,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Has the night descended?<br />
  Was the road of late so toilsome? did we stop discouraged nodding<br />
<span class='indent' /> on our way?<br />
  Yet a passing hour I yield you in your tracks to pause oblivious,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!

<span class='indent' /> Till with sound of trumpet,<br />
  Far, far off the daybreak call hark! how loud and clear I hear it wind,<br />
  Swift! to the head of the army! swift! spring to your places,<br />
<span class='indent' /> Pioneers! O pioneers!




To You

  Whoever you are, I fear you are walking the walks of dreams,<br />
  I fear these supposed realities are to melt from under your feet and hands,<br />
  Even now your features, joys, speech, house, trade, manners,<br />
<span class='indent' />troubles, follies, costume, crimes, dissipate away from you,<br />
  Your true soul and body appear before me.<br />
  They stand forth out of affairs, out of commerce, shops, work,<br />
<span class='indent' />farms, clothes, the house, buying, selling, eating, drinking,<br />
<span class='indent' />suffering, dying.

  Whoever you are, now I place my hand upon you, that you be my poem,<br />
  I whisper with my lips close to your ear.<br />
  I have loved many women and men, but I love none better than you.

  O I have been dilatory and dumb,<br />
  I should have made my way straight to you long ago,<br />
  I should have blabb'd nothing but you, I should have chanted nothing<br />
<span class='indent' />but you.

  I will leave all and come and make the hymns of you,<br />
  None has understood you, but I understand you,<br />
  None has done justice to you, you have not done justice to yourself,<br />
  None but has found you imperfect, I only find no imperfection in you,<br />
  None but would subordinate you, I only am he who will never consent<br />
<span class='indent' />to subordinate you,<br />
  I only am he who places over you no master, owner, better, God,<br />
<span class='indent' />beyond what waits intrinsically in yourself.

  Painters have painted their swarming groups and the centre-figure of all,<br />
  From the head of the centre-figure spreading a nimbus of gold-color'd light,<br />
  But I paint myriads of heads, but paint no head without its nimbus<br />
<span class='indent' />of gold-color'd light,<br />
  From my hand from the brain of every man and woman it streams,<br />
<span class='indent' />effulgently flowing forever.

  O I could sing such grandeurs and glories about you!<br />
  You have not known what you are, you have slumber'd upon yourself<br />
<span class='indent' />all your life,<br />
  Your eyelids have been the same as closed most of the time,<br />
  What you have done returns already in mockeries,<br />
  (Your thrift, knowledge, prayers, if they do not return in<br />
<span class='indent' />mockeries, what is their return?)

  The mockeries are not you,<br />
  Underneath them and within them I see you lurk,<br />
  I pursue you where none else has pursued you,<br />
  Silence, the desk, the flippant expression, the night, the<br />
<span class='indent' />accustom'd routine, if these conceal you from others or from<br />
<span class='indent' />yourself, they do not conceal you from me,<br />
  The shaved face, the unsteady eye, the impure complexion, if these<br />
<span class='indent' />balk others they do not balk me,<br />
  The pert apparel, the deform'd attitude, drunkenness, greed,<br />
<span class='indent' />premature death, all these I part aside.

  There is no endowment in man or woman that is not tallied in you,<br />
  There is no virtue, no beauty in man or woman, but as good is in you,<br />
  No pluck, no endurance in others, but as good is in you,<br />
  No pleasure waiting for others, but an equal pleasure waits for you.

  As for me, I give nothing to any one except I give the like carefully<br />
<span class='indent' />to you,<br />
  I sing the songs of the glory of none, not God, sooner than I sing<br />
<span class='indent' />the songs of the glory of you.

  Whoever you are! claim your own at any hazard!<br />
  These shows of the East and West are tame compared to you,<br />
  These immense meadows, these interminable rivers, you are immense<br />
<span class='indent' />and interminable as they,<br />
  These furies, elements, storms, motions of Nature, throes of apparent<br />
<span class='indent' />dissolution, you are he or she who is master or mistress over them,<br />
  Master or mistress in your own right over Nature, elements, pain,<br />
<span class='indent' />passion, dissolution.

  The hopples fall from your ankles, you find an unfailing sufficiency,<br />
  Old or young, male or female, rude, low, rejected by the rest,<br />
<span class='indent' />whatever you are promulges itself,<br />
  Through birth, life, death, burial, the means are provided, nothing<br />
<span class='indent' />is scanted,<br />
  Through angers, losses, ambition, ignorance, ennui, what you are<br />
<span class='indent' />picks its way.




France [the 18th Year of these States

  A great year and place<br />
  A harsh discordant natal scream out-sounding, to touch the mother's<br />
<span class='indent' />heart closer than any yet.

  I walk'd the shores of my Eastern sea,<br />
  Heard over the waves the little voice,<br />
  Saw the divine infant where she woke mournfully wailing, amid the<br />
<span class='indent' />roar of cannon, curses, shouts, crash of falling buildings,<br />
  Was not so sick from the blood in the gutters running, nor from the single<br />
<span class='indent' />corpses, nor those in heaps, nor those borne away in the tumbrils,<br />
  Was not so desperate at the battues of death was not so shock'd at<br />
<span class='indent' />the repeated fusillades of the guns.

  Pale, silent, stern, what could I say to that long-accrued retribution?<br />
  Could I wish humanity different?<br />
  Could I wish the people made of wood and stone?<br />
  Or that there be no justice in destiny or time?

  O Liberty! O mate for me!<br />
  Here too the blaze, the grape-shot and the axe, in reserve, to fetch<br />
<span class='indent' />them out in case of need,<br />
  Here too, though long represt, can never be destroy'd,<br />
  Here too could rise at last murdering and ecstatic,<br />
  Here too demanding full arrears of vengeance.

  Hence I sign this salute over the sea,<br />
  And I do not deny that terrible red birth and baptism,<br />
  But remember the little voice that I heard wailing, and wait with<br />
<span class='indent' />perfect trust, no matter how long,<br />
  And from to-day sad and cogent I maintain the bequeath'd cause, as<br />
<span class='indent' />for all lands,<br />
  And I send these words to Paris with my love,<br />
  And I guess some chansonniers there will understand them,<br />
  For I guess there is latent music yet in France, floods of it,<br />
  O I hear already the bustle of instruments, they will soon be<br />
<span class='indent' />drowning all that would interrupt them,<br />
  O I think the east wind brings a triumphal and free march,<br />
  It reaches hither, it swells me to Joyful madness,<br />
  I will run transpose it in words, to justify<br />
  I will yet sing a song for you ma femme.




Myself and Mine

  Myself and mine gymnastic ever,<br />
  To stand the cold or heat, to take good aim with a gun, to sail a<br />
<span class='indent' />boat, to manage horses, to beget superb children,<br />
  To speak readily and clearly, to feel at home among common people,<br />
  And to hold our own in terrible positions on land and sea.

  Not for an embroiderer,<br />
  (There will always be plenty of embroiderers, I welcome them also,)<br />
  But for the fibre of things and for inherent men and women.

  Not to chisel ornaments,<br />
  But to chisel with free stroke the heads and limbs of plenteous<br />
<span class='indent' />supreme Gods, that the States may realize them walking and talking.

  Let me have my own way,<br />
  Let others promulge the laws, I will make no account of the laws,<br />
  Let others praise eminent men and hold up peace, I hold up agitation<br />
<span class='indent' />and conflict,<br />
  I praise no eminent man, I rebuke to his face the one that was<br />
<span class='indent' />thought most worthy.

  (Who are you? and what are you secretly guilty of all your life?<br />
  Will you turn aside all your life? will you grub and chatter all<br />
<span class='indent' />your life?<br />
  And who are you, blabbing by rote, years, pages, languages, reminiscences,<br />
  Unwitting to-day that you do not know how to speak properly a single word?)

  Let others finish specimens, I never finish specimens,<br />
  I start them by exhaustless laws as Nature does, fresh and modern<br />
<span class='indent' />continually.

  I give nothing as duties,<br />
  What others give as duties I give as living impulses,<br />
  (Shall I give the heart's action as a duty?)

  Let others dispose of questions, I dispose of nothing, I arouse<br />
<span class='indent' />unanswerable questions,<br />
  Who are they I see and touch, and what about them?<br />
  What about these likes of myself that draw me so close by tender<br />
<span class='indent' />directions and indirections?

  I call to the world to distrust the accounts of my friends, but<br />
<span class='indent' />listen to my enemies, as I myself do,<br />
  I charge you forever reject those who would expound me, for I cannot<br />
<span class='indent' />expound myself,<br />
  I charge that there be no theory or school founded out of me,<br />
  I charge you to leave all free, as I have left all free.

  After me, vista!<br />
  O I see life is not short, but immeasurably long,<br />
  I henceforth tread the world chaste, temperate, an early riser, a<br />
<span class='indent' />steady grower,<br />
  Every hour the semen of centuries, and still of centuries.

  I must follow up these continual lessons of the air, water, earth,<br />
  I perceive I have no time to lose.




Year of Meteors [1859-60

  Year of meteors! brooding year!<br />
  I would bind in words retrospective some of your deeds and signs,<br />
  I would sing your contest for the 19th Presidentiad,<br />
  I would sing how an old man, tall, with white hair, mounted the<br />
<span class='indent' />scaffold in Virginia,<br />
  (I was at hand, silent I stood with teeth shut close, I watch'd,<br />
  I stood very near you old man when cool and indifferent, but trembling<br />
<span class='indent' />with age and your unheal'd wounds you mounted the scaffold;)<br />
  I would sing in my copious song your census returns of the States,<br />
  The tables of population and products, I would sing of your ships<br />
<span class='indent' />and their cargoes,<br />
  The proud black ships of Manhattan arriving, some fill'd with<br />
<span class='indent' />immigrants, some from the isthmus with cargoes of gold,<br />
  Songs thereof would I sing, to all that hitherward comes would welcome give,<br />
  And you would I sing, fair stripling! welcome to you from me, young<br />
<span class='indent' />prince of England!<br />
  (Remember you surging Manhattan's crowds as you pass'd with your<br />
<span class='indent' />cortege of nobles?<br />
  There in the crowds stood I, and singled you out with attachment;)<br />
  Nor forget I to sing of the wonder, the ship as she swam up my bay,<br />
  Well-shaped and stately the Great Eastern swam up my bay, she was<br />
<span class='indent' />600 feet long,<br />
  Her moving swiftly surrounded by myriads of small craft I forget not<br />
<span class='indent' />to sing;<br />
  Nor the comet that came unannounced out of the north flaring in heaven,<br />
  Nor the strange huge meteor-procession dazzling and clear shooting<br />
<span class='indent' />over our heads,<br />
  (A moment, a moment long it sail'd its balls of unearthly light over<br />
<span class='indent' />our heads,<br />
  Then departed, dropt in the night, and was gone;)<br />
  Of such, and fitful as they, I sing with gleams from them would<br />
<span class='indent' />gleam and patch these chants,<br />
  Your chants, O year all mottled with evil and good year of forebodings!<br />
  Year of comets and meteors transient and strange lo! even here one<br />
<span class='indent' />equally transient and strange!<br />
  As I flit through you hastily, soon to fall and be gone, what is this chant,<br />
  What am I myself but one of your meteors?




With Antecedents

<span class='indent' /> 1<br />
  With antecedents,<br />
  With my fathers and mothers and the accumulations of past ages,<br />
